Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 Afterward, cure the wound as has been said before, and let the cautery be of three grains in the following form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And therefore, the cauteries are lighter, because you make three of them at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	about the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterward, have the patient recline on their back and side; afterward, lift the heart that is within the chest with the tips of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery that has two nerves, such is its form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces to the ribcage, and the figure of the cautery would come together as four cauteries; and for this reason, the cautery is made with the cautery that has three nerves, so that the figure of cauterization is six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the delicacy of a tent and such is the form of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is adjusted on this one nerve so that there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterward, place the powdered cautery that has been boiled with oil on top; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is fully healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated above, and little has happened, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cautery handle, or apply many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When cold and moisture come to the stomach, causing it to become imbalanced, and phlegm multiplies in it, and the usual cures are not effective, then the patient should be positioned on their back with extended legs and arms.[Repeated text from earlier has been omitted]
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 Of this later, I perform three fire cauteries: one beneath the cupping glass of the breast, of a finger's length, with the entire cautery nail; and two cauteries outside the two ribs, such that the figure of the cauteries is at three angles, and there is sufficient space between them so that they will not join together when they are laid down for putrefaction; and let the cauteries be of such depth that they penetrate both parts of the flesh, with the figure of the cauteries being according to this form without deviation.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form, and one is fearful of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and pressing down on the stomach at one point according to the quantity that you desire; then cauterize with the entire cautery which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the care of the wound that we had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	 As for liver pain caused by cold and moisture and excessive flatulence, which makes it deviate from its natural composition due to excesses; and the patient is not relieved by the treatments we have mentioned in divisions, then the patient should be frequently placed on a heated bed; and place three cauteries according to this form, figure, and quantity on the liver, beyond the hypochondria, where the ribs meet; and leave a space between each cautery as large as a thumb; and let the cauteries be long in size, but not too tight with your hand; and only burn half of the liver, and let the patient be lying down on their feet; and if they cannot do this, then let them lie down, extend their legs, and raise their arms; and this is the method:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And if you wish, cauterize these cauteries with the scalpel, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and take care not to burn the whole heart, for you would make the entire body dry out; and let it not boil, because the heart is very delicate in that area, and be careful about this.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient will feel not too much pain; and if it is in the membrane, the pain will be intense.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And when this treatment should be administered by the physicians, it is necessary that the patient be positioned with their head raised; and then bind the area where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a grape, of which this is the shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 And cauterize with the cautery until the core is burned and comes to suppuration, so that all pus is expelled; then treat it according to the treatment of wounds until it heals; and it is not appropriate for anyone except those who have studied medicine for a long time and cured such illnesses several times to use this cautery.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can boldly work, and yet it seems to me that moving (the dislocation) is better than leaving it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the pleurisy cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauteries for pleurisy with aristolochia roots, and in this manner: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your fingers; and moisten it in oil, and hold it in the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries a little below in the area that is beneath the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining a little behind; and one in the armpit, and one on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the chest beyond the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but instead make it open as if you were smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And some ancient (person) said that certain men use the fire cautery like a razor, heating it and placing it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and then, if the pain departs, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work, there is fear that the patient may die immediately or a fistula may develop which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse (or mites)
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the "mice" (or mites) in those that I have mentioned in the divisions of cures, and it does not help at all, then there are three kinds of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 Of these, one method is that you make III or IV cauteries, in a row according to the length of the member, according to the figure of the liver cautery that we have said before; and do not press your hand onto the entire cautery, and let the patient be lying on their back; and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has II nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the chest which is opposite the member, where the patient's ribs come towards the left, and let the lifting of the chest be according to the chest, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 After insert the two heated nerves until the core is pierced on the other side, then pull out the cautery, and in this way there will be four holes. And if you wish, cauterize with the entire cautery up to three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 After the cure, when it has putrefied for a long time, and this is worth than the other cures mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 The cautery is not suitable for the hydroptic (person with dropsy), except for the method called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 When you cure according to the methods that we have mentioned in divisions and your cure does not help at all, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back on the spine, and one near the side; and let the cauteries be close to the thickness of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery to smolder for a long time, and do not stop the care of the patient after the cautery; and if healing is hurried, the two intentions will come together with the help of God. de l’enfleure des piez	of inflammation of the feet

When the feet are swollen in a person who is dropsical, and are filled with yellow fluid, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning it.

Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy part which is called "thigh"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the thigh, heat the fire-brand that looks like a razor, and then place it all glowing hot on the cut thigh; leave your hand there until the brand reaches the base of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of flesh, cauterize each part as we have said; after that, use wound-healing treatments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large fire-brand made of alum, it will be of greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of an improperly treated wound

When the patient cannot tolerate surgery or incision (which we will discuss later), then there comes a disease that can only be healed by cauterization.

se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu. de la dolor de la hainche	for hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the joint of the hip, and it is caused by coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated for this as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of heavy humors with stinking pills, or other good similar ones.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 Afterward, perform cautery; and the methods of cautery are of two kinds: namely, heating medications and fire cautery.

Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars. And if necessary, more are done; and if they know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then a knife-like or circular cautery is done, and be careful in all your cauteries to not leave the cautery on for so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen several who made a fire cautery on the ankle of the foot and left it on until the leg was completely swollen, and the foot as well, and the whole foot became pierced and corrupted.

Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a cure in which a man was cured of the pain of inflammation and sciatic nerve, and he praised it highly, and said that no other cure was made, and that he was cured at once when this cure was made, and he bathed himself as instructed hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he says in this manner that you should take fresh and dry litharge (lead monoxide), and grind it well with a little fat, and apply it to the inflammation and to the thigh and to the leg where the pain resides, and bind it; and let it stay for 3 hours, and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then have him enter the bath until his body is slightly invigorated, and have him enter the bed, and the pain will completely go away and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 And know that no one should use such a fire cautery unless it is after the evacuation of humors.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Dioscorides said that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it is very helpful; and the cautery should be done in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called fascia.[References to anatomical structures have been modernized for clarity.]
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 Afterwards, take dry goat's rennet, heat it over fire until it becomes charcoal, place it on wool and leave it until it cools down; and repeat this process until you think that it has reached the inflammation (hainche), and the pain has ceased; and this method of cauterization is called "cautery of goat's rennet".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or being struck, or from excessive bleeding, or from the spreading of cold matter, none of these instances is appropriate for cauterization, except in the case of one caused by the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient has been purged with foul-smelling pills or similar treatments, three lines be signed on the back, in the area where the pain is located, using incense; and within each line, five cauterizations or more should be made, depending on the strength and quantity that the patient can tolerate; and let the cauterization be done using the type of cauterization called "poins"; and if you wish, make three or four cauterizations using the clavile moien technique, in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have stiff necks when they get up, and fear; and you will find on the last spine in the back, and the appearance which comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see these signs and wish to cure them, cauterize with the cautery of this type, in this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 Such that the cautery affects each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointing two or three lines (in distance) and let the points be close to each other.[This sentence is recommending that if the medical practitioner wants to cauterize around the spine, they should do so by making sure the cautery tool touches the skin at a distance of 2 or 3 lines away from the spine, with the points being placed closely together.]
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 Afterwards, keep the area clean until it has healed, as we have said; and beware to not apply cautery to gout in a nerve sprain.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is due to moisture spread throughout the entire body, and when it occurs in the feet, which is called "gout" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, then it can be treated with cautery in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let them be olive-shaped, as follows:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary for you to operate on the sole of the foot, apply the cautery to the entire sole, which is called "all-point.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pains extend to the knees and other joints, which happens frequently, apply cautery to each knee three or four times on every part, using the entire olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do so, but do not hold your hand over it until the flesh is completely burned.[Note: I am a language model and my translations should be used as a starting point and verified by a professional translation service or native speaker. The spelling and grammar of Old French has many variations and the text may contain errors.]
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there is no more pain in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care to the patient and give them medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 Because if you take good care of them and purge phlegm, they will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the syphilis sore.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the abscess comes to a head and the bowels descend to the hips and it is recent, then when you see to cure it, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that empty the belly, so that the feces descend from their belly; after make them sit on their back between your hands, and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has receded, and press gently with your fingers around the abscess on the bone of the wrist, and make a sign like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the shape: [Here a picture/diagram would follow in the original text]
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 until it is white and excretes pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 Then return the bowels to their place; and the minister places his hand so that they do not return backward; and works well the thighs for the patient, and puts a cushion and a sergeant under the thighs, and another on the side who holds his hands; then place the cautery on the mark with your whole hand, and hold it right and steady until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again a second time until you come to the bone; and carefully watch that the boil does not burst when you apply the cautery; so as not to burn him; and so that through this the patient does not die, or suffers other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And it is necessary that the cautery for children be fine according to the size of an egg, and for adults also as large according to their measure; after three days cure the wound of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; after curing other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on long enough, so that the boils do not come out when he moves to get up.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, provide him with a well-made belt and let him wear it for forty more days; and have good rest, that he works little and guards himself from excessive consumption of drink and food, and from high jumps; and when he follows this teaching, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I will say hereafter the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of abdominal surgery
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When ruptures come in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow anymore, perform the fire cautery of the reont cautery according to its size, and burn one third of the core; then cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with the three-angled cautery in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the location of the incision and make a line along the width above the rupture, and another below, and place your hand in the middle of the entire cauterizing claw.[Note: I am not sure about the translation of "clavile" in this context. It could also be translated as "clasp" or "clamp".]
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cautery is lighter and subtler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in some member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes to any limb, either from falling or injury, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the treatments of medicine are of no use, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the "pointed" cautery, and let the cautery be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and strength, and its location in terms of twists and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 If it heals from the first cautery, that is good; but if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for it is often the case that it must change to the member that is close by, therefore you should continue with the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The eyelids are sometimes helped by cautery with great aid, and likewise the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 If you wish to cauterize, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and it does not subside or remain, and you doubt that corruption may spread throughout the patient; then perform V cauteries on the head: one at the crown of the head, and another toward the forehead at the end of the hairline; and II on the two temples, and I behind on the nape; and leave your hand in place so that the cautery reaches the bone, and for as long as the scabs come out, so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize on the muscle according to what is beforehand.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the diseased place is spread out everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the following cauteries that we have mentioned in the head: one cautery on the nose, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, six cauteries on the spine of the back, one large one on the hip and another next to it, two on the shoulders, two on the elbows, two on the knees of the legs, one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are at the back of the heel so as not to burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the thumb, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more I do with fire cautery, the more help I give, and movement it promotes; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already thoroughly weakened.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And the cautery should be large or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the ways of ironwork.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Afterwards, apply to it a mixture of bran flour, honey, and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When swelling comes to any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then cauterize the limb according to its size; and let the cauter be slightly into the thickness of the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes, a cautery is performed on the hand, foot, and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and in this way, swelling is removed; yet no one should interfere if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	I'm not sure what you're asking. The term "de albaras" does not appear in the Old French medical text provided earlier. Could you please clarify your request or provide more context? I'll be happy to help further.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has become advanced and the means of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the size of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and the color changed; then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of a rooster and pigeon, each in equal parts; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and expose it to air until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of cancer (or more accurately, "chancre") by cautery refers to the use of hot metal instruments to burn or destroy diseased tissue. This was a common medical practice in medieval times due to the lack of effective surgical techniques and anesthetics. Here's a possible line-by-line translation:
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When a chancre first appears and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that is circular, all around the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 And yet, wise men say that one should also perform cautery in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen before; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around the edge with a "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot grow
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has an illness called "adubelati", and it delays in killing or due to the excess it makes, or due to the water of the sick person when they are infirm (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to time; and you wish to hasten its death: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 because it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery like this: (followed by a description of shaping the cautery)
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And put your hand in the middle of this illness called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and make such cauteries that the patient feels them outside in such a way that the course of the gangrene is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the care until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another kind of illness exists which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing but a consuming disease of the limbs, for it consumes the limbs just as fire consumes dry logs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 If you see this disease in a place that can tolerate the application of a hot cautery, then heat the cautery rod slowly and gradually, according to the location where the disease is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all the corruption, and let nothing of it remain, so that everything corrupt be removed.[*](note: "cauterize" here means to burn or sear the skin with a hot iron or other instrument, in order to destroy diseased tissue. It was a common medical practice in medieval times)
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then let it [the affected area] rest for three days, and place crushed cabbage with oil on the cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are removed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After treating [the wound] with medications that produce flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if after three days you see that healthy flesh is not growing, that is good; and if not, then reapply the cautery on those parts of the wound that have remained corrupt.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 And this condition has at times been cured by medication instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is of greater help. I have already mentioned the cure for this medication in the previous section: take it when needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the corns that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 Much it happens that in the feet is born a disease called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large swollen thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cauteries for this disease are of two kinds.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, the fire cautery, and the cautery of hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 The fire cautery is that you heat the cautery like a vault pen, and it should be made of good iron to the measure that can touch the nail from all sides, and it should have fine edges; then place it very hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the base of the nail; and leave it in this way for three days until it begins to rot; then make a plaster of crushed mallows with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the wound with a swelling of flesh by making it clean.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if they are turned inward by the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done in this manner: take an iron or copper rod, or a pen of vaults, and place the nail and the styptic, that is to say powdered verdigris; and place the rod so that it surrounds completely, then put some hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the rod comes to the base of the nail, and can find a deep path through the hot water to the base; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will detach completely with its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 Do one after the other, as you burn all those that are on the body, then cure the inflammations that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	I would translate "li cure dou trembler" as "the treatment for trembling".
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble from cold nerves or quartan fever or other causes, then you should make four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one in the foot, and one on the stomach at the olive cautionery; this will stop the trembling, and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of smelly pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes it happens that the body appears with bare spots, or putrid pustules, which come from thick corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 It is necessary, at the first sign of them, to apply a fire cautery on each pustule: a subtle probe made of myrtle wood, with its tip heated in the fire, or a long root of aristolochia, or a round-shaped cautery.[it is interesting that this medieval medical treatise suggests using myrtle wood or aristolochia roots as tools for cauterization. Myrtle wood was known to have medicinal properties and was used in ancient times for various purposes such as wound healing and pain relief. Aristolochia, on the other hand, is a plant genus that contains many toxic compounds. It's use in medicine has been controversial due to its potential harmful effects. The round-shaped cautery referred to here may be a type of medical instrument used for cauterization, which could be made of various materials such as iron, copper or bronze.]
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but the superfluidities from which they come are broken off, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	It often happens that there is great loss of blood from the artery which is cut in the wound, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop [the bleeding].
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, hurry to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press very hard so that the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more drips from it; then heat various olive-shaped cauteries, both large and small, until they are all red; then take one, whether large or small, according to the size and location of the wound in which the artery is cut, and place the cautery on this vein where you have your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your hand above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take another one quickly from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and take care not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood runs from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially if the artery is large, unless it is through one of the four ways that we have said: through cauterization, or through extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop blood; and let it be bound and constricted appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	One who will administer stopping the bleeding by tightly binding with bandages or placing hot things on it, or similar things, will not help much.[Original text is in Medieval French, and I am providing a translation into Modern English.]
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone who does not have any remedy or medicine present, then they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it stops bleeding over the wound and over the vein; and they must not move it, but moisten it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make preparations for what they need in terms of cautery and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and described the operations, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have placed the chapter on fevers from head to foot, and I will go in this chapter along the same path so that one may more easily find what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this one, it is important, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I advise you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 There are those who are so afflicted by their illness that they would easily die from the force of its severity and the greatness of its wickedness; and one should fear for these individuals.[Translate]
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And there are those who regain consciousness and say, "wait, I am cured"; yet their illness is contemptuous.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 It is not appropriate for you to agree with those who come to you with this behavior, but rather put more effort into your honor than your greed, and do not rashly but wisely open up to those about whom you are certain, and from whom you can gain both profit and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients for their health to be restored; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, May our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to breathe in the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	And I have arranged this chapter for you, dividing it into sections according to what is before the chapter on cauteries, which I have described from head to foot, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a swollen head filled with water.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes very often to children at birth, and when the womb constrains the child's head too forcefully; and sometimes it happens for no known reason.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen, death came quickly; and for this reason, it seems to me that it would be better to abandon such treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child in whom the head was filled with water, and the head grew heavier each day until it could no longer be supported; and the moisture increased so much that he died, and this moisture is collected under the bone above the hip, between the pelvis and the bone. The treatment for this condition is as follows if the moisture is between the pelvis and the bone, and the abscess is small: make an incision in the head, wide enough to allow the moisture to drain out; it should be at least two fingers long, depending on where the moisture is located. Here is the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, as shown below:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are that the corners of the chin spread apart from each other in every part, and fluid comes out when you press it with your hand from the inside, and this does not heal: then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision, remove all the moisture thoroughly.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 Afterwards, bind the wounds with cloth and powders, and put wine and oil on it, and leave it like that until the fifth day; then loosen it and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and also keep the head bound, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe where the swelling of the abscess appears and the gathering of water, for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes to the right, and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut there where the abscess is visible and the gathering of water, in a manner according to your ability; and be careful not to cut the artery; and if blood flows from it, so that the patient dies from bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of a rupture (or swelling)
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When a person becomes ill with a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or the feet, and the illness is chronic and not helped by medical treatment, then the last resort is the fire cautery; this will involve burning two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 Then, when you cover the eyes, let the patient bend his head back; after that, rub the area around his ear with a rough cloth until the arteries appear; then, have the patient pull his neck tight with the entire cloth; then look for where the veins protrude, and the places on either side of the ears are swollen; then mark those spots; then cut both veins with a lancet sharpened on both sides, so that the incision reaches the bone, and this should be done at the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see (that) the artery, place the sharp spatula under it and cut above it, making two incisions crosswise, like a pair of dice.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood will spurt out continuously.[ISI] Et se tu voes que il en sant pas assez, puis esforce le col du malaide au dela de l’espaule et si li frotte le chief et les espaules a un drapel ardant; et se ceo ne li valt riens, si copes la grant artère qui est entre les deux espaulx.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And if the artery does not appear upon touch, then measure a space of three fingers' width and make an incision to the bone; and the amount of blood that must be let is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can withstand and the fullness of the artery; then observe the wound: if pus remains on the bone tip of the styptic, cut it away so that no abscess forms, then close and bind the wound, and treat it with ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	"de grains" in this context likely refers to small grains or seeds. A possible interpretation could be "six grains," which would indicate a measurement of volume, similar to how one might use rice or lentils as a unit of measurement today. However, it is not clear what specific type of grain is meant by "de emigrainne" in this medieval medical text.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When there is an old chronic headache and acute catarrh, caused by moisture in the tears and heat in the temples, and a swollen and insane forehead and similar things, and this condition has been treated with various medical cures without success, then we should draw blood from the temples and cauterize the area. This is what we have described before.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The method for extracting the blood from the temples is as follows: the patient should part their hair and pay attention to the artery that is visible in the temple, which can easily be felt due to its pulsating movement. This artery is not very prominent in some people who are too cold; if it is not prominent, the patient should constrict their neck with a cloth, then rub the area with a rough cloth until the artery becomes clearly visible. Then take a lancet (spatumile) of the following shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 then gently flay the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it up with hemostats and separate it well from the membranes that are beneath it on each side; and if the artery is fine, then hook it with the tip of the probe, then cut off that part according to the quantity of the two sides.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 for if it is not cut off, the blood will not flow out at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and draw blood from the six holes, up to three; and if the artery is large, then it must be tied in two places with a sturdy double thread of silk, so that no rotting occurs before the wound heals and proper bleeding takes place; then cut away the excess that is between the two ties at that very hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize the wound with a scalpel cautery up to the bone until the holes are closed; and this is the best practice, if the patient does not have a fever and they have a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery stops moisture: therefore it is of greater help for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the area with old cotton and place well-made bandages on top; and when they are loosened, they must be treated with dry medicines that promote flesh growth, and bandages, until it heals; and if a piece of the artery is left as long as you work, then quickly cover it with a cauterizing iron, or fill the area with vitriol and press on it with your hand until the blood stops flowing; and if you don't have that present, then place your finger on the area until the blood clots, and sprinkle cold water on the area until it stops flowing, and press as needed; and the best and easiest method for extracting an artery is to cauterize the wound with this cutting cautery of two parts, but let the edges be thick so that they retain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a gap of the width of a thumb between the two blades, and when you have marked the two places to be cauterized, place the red-hot iron on it until it reaches the bone and cut the vein in two places; and keep them separate between the two edges because this cautery is not solid all around; and that is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears come from the veins above the forehead and are not relieved by any medical treatment, and you see the face of the patient become red, and feel a pulsation on the forehead as if it is trembling; and if the eyelids are tight and moist so that the paper has fallen off, and the paper has been warmed up and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And the ancients called it "cure contused," and you should do the following for the patient who has this illness: have them let their hair grow on their forehead, then make three evenly spaced incisions on their forehead according to its length; one of the incisions should be in the middle of the forehead, extending from the eyebrows down to the nose, and the other two should be at the temples; take care not to cut the arteries that are at the temples; keep your hand away from the jawline; and make each wound the length of three fingers next to each other; have ready a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping away the blood, then insert the stylet (spatumile), cut in two parts as follows:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision made above the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the flesh that is between the two cuts down to the suture on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this styptic.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	and insert into the first cut the instrument called "cultellarie", which is very sharp on one side, and on the other side it is blunt and not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And place the blunt side of the knife towards the fleshy part of the ribcage near the heart, and the sharp side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle split.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to where the heart is visible, and then make another incision in the middle split up to the other side; and then bleed evenly, and press on the area to extract blood; then place a piece of old cotton in each split, and put wet bandages on it with wine and oil and vinegar, and ensure that abscesses do not develop; and on the third day loosen the binding, and apply a large amount of cold water, then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments used for wound healing until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the swelling of the eyes
