Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone is accustomed to getting catarrh, and you see thin and small eyes, weakened vision, and burnt paper; and the hair falls out, and there is deep pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that those matters and those catarrhs do not come out but from many veins, and the proper cure for it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And instruct the patient to bend their forehead, then make a large split in the middle of the forehead, and another one of a width of an inch.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 Begin at the left temple split and continue to the right temple, cutting down to the bone; keep your hand away from the temple nerves that move when eating; once the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two lips of the split and place there an old piece of cotton and linen cloth; then apply damp cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, being careful to avoid a hot abscess; when removed, rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then cure it with drying agents that promote the growth of flesh.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner, take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colophony, and make an ointment; administer it on these wounds to help generate flesh all over.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	"de l'estoupement des oreilles" means "on ear stoppers/plugs". The term refers to the act of blocking or stopping up the ears, typically by inserting a piece of cotton or other material to prevent air or fluid from entering or escaping. This technique can be used for various purposes, such as protecting the ears during bathing, diving, or flying, relieving ear pain due to changes in pressure, or preventing water from entering the ear canal and causing infection. In a medieval medical context, ear stoppers could also be used in conjunction with distillations or other treatments for the ears.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: either grains, or animals, or mineral stones such as iron; or seeds, such as lice, beans, peas; or fluids such as water and ashes and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls into the ear a stone or any other thing that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, then expose the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see the stone, distill a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then facilitate extraction; make them sneeze using some condiment, and stop up their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and tilt the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Often, it comes out by this cure; and if it does not come out, facilitate extraction using subtle pincers, of which the form is as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out using pincers, that is good; if not, then facilitate extraction using a thin probe wire of fine double-wire. And if it does not come out this way, make a small horn of tin and place the end of the horn in the ear hole, and stop up what is around the horn with soft wax so that no air can enter with the horn; then pull hard, as often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take birdlime and apply some to an instrument made for this purpose, and place a piece of cotton around; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out using any of the things we have mentioned, then hurry to lance the ear so that abscess and hardening may occur, as well as spasm; and the manner of lancing is such that you should first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to their strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upward, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty tissue or flesh; and let the incision be like a crescent moon, coming to the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck it out with your mouth; and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inflamed, administer extraction; and if it cannot go out, then use a thin spatula of this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision into that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not make incisions when you think the gland is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces of it; then carefully extract and assist with forceps, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 Therefore, in the water that falls in the ear, the patient should use sneezing herbs first and widen the ear with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And lie on the same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it comes out by itself because of this, it is good.[NOTE: The pronoun "ceu" here refers to the use of sneezing herbs and lying on the ear, which was mentioned in the previous sentences.]
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If not, take many small and light pebbles, warm them slightly by the fire, and place one or two of them in the patient's ear where the water is. Then jump on it with your feet from the other side, and strike another stone against the stone in the ear, and do not stop striking one stone against another until all the water comes out, and it will all come out; and if you wish, take a reed, and insert one end into the ear, and light the other end with fire until the larger part of the reed is burned; then repeat this process with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said with stones.[NOTE: The text suggests using pebbles or a reed to create heat in the ear canal to help evaporate the water inside. This method may not be recommended today as it could potentially cause harm to the ear.]
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is of small size, such as a louse and similar things, cure it as we have said in division (?); but if it is of large size that can be felt, then administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and treatment of distillations, and the cure is not effective, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if you see any visible worms, then carefully remove them with tweezers, and if you don't see any, then take a probe of the kind described here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And should be tight below and loose above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And insert the sharpest end of the instrument into the ear according to the level of discomfort of the patient, then strongly pull on the entire chain; do this frequently until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not obey to come out, then stop up the chain with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not emerge as we have said, then administer the tested distillations that the ancients used in cases of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear by means of this instrument, so here is its form as you see.[translation varied to match subject]
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or bronze, narrow below with a small hole, and wide above for distillation; and have a well-made bronze instrument to press the distillation inside, and if you wish, take a spoon and wrap cotton around its tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you want in the cannula, while keeping it inside the ear; then insert the spoon with all the cotton, and gently press your hand until the oil is distilled or comes out of the ear; let the patient feel the sensation inside, and let the distillation be a small pot heated by fire so that it can be distilled in the ear; and make sure it is not too cold, as the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	"de l'estoupement des oreilles" means "on ear stoppers/plugs". The term refers to the act of blocking or stopping up the ears, typically by inserting a piece of cotton or other material to prevent air or fluid from entering or escaping. This technique can be used for various purposes, such as protecting the ears during bathing, diving, or flying, relieving ear pain due to changes in pressure, or preventing water from entering the ear canal and causing infection. In a medieval medical context, ear stoppers could also be used in conjunction with distillations or other treatments for the ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	Any child is born who has no holes in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to blockage from wound or pus inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes goes deep into the ear, if it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small hole visible near the hole, and one can see it.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one then that goes deep, if it cannot be seen, is of difficult healing in many cases, and in the one that can be seen, it is necessary that you expose the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the blockage apparent, work on it immediately with this tool, as described in the following form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind, so that it does not wound the ear; if the blockage is from pus or flesh in the ear, hold it with fine forceps and gently scrape it until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if pus is deep within the ear, take a thin, sharp razor, heat it slightly over fire, then place it in the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you notice pus causing discomfort to the patient upon hearing, make a small incision while taking care not to harm the ear's nerves; then insert a wick into the ear canal according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for some days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder on top of vitriol broken; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you draw the tent and apply another tent soaked in cerote made of oil rose and wax, as long as the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, then soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that remove the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	Here is the translation:
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This eye-healing salve that comes in paper when the eyes are moist and dry, it is necessary to stretch them with pliers and tweezers, and cut some of its roots with a spatula; then put vitriol powder on top of it.[References:](https://www.pinterest.com/pin/547328963015833448/)
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it is not possible to cut it out, cauterize it with a subtle lenticular cautery, and after the incision, move the cauterizer; and many times they heal, when some things still remain of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burnt and do not return at all.
de la gresle	Of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Often, small hardened particles that resemble grains in shape and texture appear on the paper-like membranes of the eyes, which is why this condition is called "grain"; it consists of a gathering of thick moisture on the membrane's surface and underside. The treatment is as follows: observe if the grain moves from one side to another, which is an easy thing to determine; then make an incision around it and carefully scrape each side, then use forceps to grasp and remove it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 if you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, it does not harm the patient; and if the wound is large, suture it with stitches and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for the ointment will soon restore it and help heal the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the gravel is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper and stretch the gravel with tweezers, and cut it and press it from one side and another; and if the paper is separated by incision, it does not harm; and when the gravel is cut, rinse the eye with saline solution, and cure the wound of anything that harms flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 Exinach is an ointment that is smeared on parchment paper, and this happens more in children than in any other people, and it greatly irritates their eyes, and they get runny noses in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because their tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason, they often lie on their backs with their faces up and sleep, and their parchment papers are moist under their eyebrows, which causes swelling and gives the appearance of exinach in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the outeryndix (exirnach) move apart.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the procedure is as follows: the patient places their head over your sanitary place; then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach present on each part, then place it on top of it; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach is gathered into the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moisture with a small knife, not wider than the wound made for bloodletting; and cut the leather deep enough to reach the exinach; and in several ways, the exinach comes out of the incision, in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract it with a piece of cloth between your fingers and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and make sure not to touch the incision, not to reach all the way to the eye, so that you do not wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not appear at the beginning of the cut, slightly increase the cut legibly until it appears; then pull it out as we have said, then moisten bandages in oil and water, and place it on the wound, and bind it with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And if there are such men who crush ice and apply it to corrupt the moisture that has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if a hot abscess comes to the joint, then treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.[Note: The word "emplaustres" is spelled as "emplastres" in some versions of this text. It refers to soft poultices or plasters applied to the skin.]
des poilz des papieres	"of the hairs of papers"
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on papers that are not natural and are old, they harm the eyes and cause various kinds of illnesses such as excessive tearing, softening of the eyelids, and inflammation, to the point that it can lead to eye destruction. And there are four ways to cure this: either by cautery with fire or by a soothing medicine according to what is described in the chapter on cautery, and this can be done through incision and stitching or bandaging, depending on what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, insert a needle with a thread on it; and let this be beside the edge of the paper where the hairs grow next to these hairs, and pull one thread above the entire paper, and turn it to the razor; then make an incision beneath the paper, beneath the adjusted hairs, up to the entire width, from the large tear duct down to the small one; then pull one thread and place underneath the paper a small cotton and linen tent, then sign on the paper a figure like a myrtle leaf, and nonetheless it is necessary that the figure corresponds to the height that you see raised the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And if there are those who need to make an incision of significant size in the paper as it has softened; then make an incision along the entire length of the spatula indicated by two lines, starting from the large tear until small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs, about the thickness of a root, then insert the probe into one of the angles of the corner and scrape it clean; then bring the two lips together with a stitch using a fine woolen thread and wipe off the blood; and if you wish, you can apply gluey substances to the eyebrows, or not; then leave the stitch and threads for three or four days; then treat the wound without drying or constricting agents, because the paper will swell upon the healing of the wound and bring it together, but the stitches are harmful (as old men say), and this is a procedure without fear; and there is another method: which is to mark the paper with a figure similar to a myrtle leaf, divided into three sections as follows:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what protrudes with small force equally according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you do not have the power to hold the pincers, and the thing is not even, take a needle with a thread, and place it in the middle of the wound; and put another thread next to the large notch, and the second thread next to the small one, and align the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have made the mark, as we have told; then bring the two edges of the wound together with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, calm it with a compress and similar soothing ointment; and it sometimes happens that the hairs of the skin turn around: you should use what we have said about the incision; but the stitches on one side and the other are more refined.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of keloids is as follows: and it is that you turn the paper (scalp) and make an incision according to what I have said, and then make two incisions with skill, and two thin threads as long as the paper and as wide as the width of the spatula; and cut the two corners of the two sides where you hold the threads; then join them gently on top of the paper above the eye, and pull the two threads firmly from both sides; and leave it like this for several days, and the skin that is pulled will die, blacken, and rot until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it delays, strike it with force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the paper is removed, and the hairs will no longer prickle; and this is the shape of the two sinews that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the work is as follows: take a thin needle and thread a soft and fine strand of silk; then bring together the edges (of the wound) and tie the threads together gently, and let the length of the threads be a palm's length; then place another fine thread of silk in the groove and tie the ends of the thread; then have the patient put his head in your lap; and do this in such a way that the work is well-lit, for it is delicate and fine work; then insert the needle into the root of the hair next to the wound, and make it pass through the paper quickly until you draw it over the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the groove, and insert the pulled-out hairs into the groove, whether there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand back so that all of the hairs come out at the groove with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the groove is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will pull the groove downwards along the thread that you have placed in it, until the groove comes out of the opening and you can see it with your eye; then you will pull the groove and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hairs stiffen in their place and new flesh grows; and if the hairs are small, then attach a long hair from the natural eyebrows to them, and lift it up with that or leave it alone, until it has become detached and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of eye ulcers (or: of eye rottenness)
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease called "alecrati" or rot comes to the eye, it is of two kinds: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly due to a wound, or from surgery or cautery, and similar things.[Note: "tailleure" here refers to a surgeon or one who performs surgical procedures.]
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And the method of treatment for it is that you cut open the scar tissue, separate its lips, and put in linen bandages, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not at all appropriate to use drying or constricting agents in its cure.[Note: "tentes de lin" refers to strips of linen cloth used for dressing wounds. The phrase "li" here refers back to the eye condition mentioned earlier.]
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 For if you do this, the illness will return worse than before; but work with softening agents, such as fenugreek; and cook the juice of lettuce or endive and flaxseed in it, and heat up some oil with dried hyssop, wrap it in a cloth, and apply it as a compress.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal in the same shape as it was before; and this work that we have mentioned is only a remedy for this disease, so that it does not return to its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This disease that is below, truly called "axacrati," and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from wounds, cracks, cautery, and similar things; and the method of the treatment is as follows: take a needle with two threads, insert it into the flesh, and pierce it from the left corner of the eye to the right, so that the threads come out in two holes of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above the needle, and cut it to the width of a span.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the form of the paper returns as it should, it is good; if not, then take a razor and place it in the split, and turn the paper, and make two splits along the edge inside the paper; and let the corners of the two splits be the two angles of the incision you have made, and make them so that when they are assembled, the form is like the shape of a letter called " Greek gamma"; then remove that flesh, according to the amount that its sides are thicker below, from what follows the paper, then join the two severed parts and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat it with what we have said about softening medicines and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a split, stitch or cauterization, then you must make a clean split in the paper under the hairs, and as it is described above; then separate between the two leaves of a bandage as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters must prepare means to the best of their ability how to make the form return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is required of labor and instruments in several dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	quickly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this bonding occurs in many people in such a way that the paper is glued to the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, so that you cut what is hard at the thin membrane (spatulum subtile), which should not be too sharp or too thick, so that the patient cannot bear that the spatula is too sharp and wounds the eye; and let your incision, by which you scrape this assembly, be light, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and let the whole assembly be healed, and do some times in the eye with salty water, and raise it with fresh water and collyrium; then put between the paper and the eye a bandage of linen, and place wet wool on the eye with plenty of egg yolk; and after three days use collyrium and other remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the toe of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the toenail can be of two types: it is nerve-like and similar to a hard callus, and another type which is not nerve-like, but rather similar to congealed white moisture. When one touches it with iron and tries to prick it with tweezers, they cannot. And both types begin near the outer corner of the eye, and grow little by little until they cover the entire vision and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient should place their head over you, then open their eyes. Lift the paper with your hand and use tweezers to pull the toenail straight. Then take a needle and put a horsehair, cow hair or buffalo hair on it, along with strong thread. Bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the toenail, piercing it all the way through with the needle. Attach the nail with a piece of thread and stretch it upwards. Then remove the skin next to the root of the nail, including the membrane and soft tissue, until you reach the base of the eyelashes, leaving the natural color or corner of the eye untouched. This way, the normal flow of tears will not be affected by the incision. Sometimes the toenail is only stretched with thread as we have described. The following is the method for removing the entire nail:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful not to let the soft tissue touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, nor let the pupil be pierced. After making the incision, put a little bit of crushed salt and a collar made from litharge into the eye and leave it there until the next day. Then cure the eye as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not sensitive, and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this similar condition of a nail is often cured with medical treatments; and they arise as I have mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, let the patient's eye look at it, and take the spatula, lightly hooked, according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And carefully retract the nail above, and if you see that it does not become thinner and the swelling approaches, distill from your mouth into the eye collyrium made of litharge and red-colored and boiled oil, and stop up the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same procedure, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If no obstacle is present in the eye, such as an abscess, then lactate it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh in the eyelid is harmful to the eye due to great injury, then suspend it with a suture, and remove part of it and not all of it, so that there is no accumulation of tears; then distill red collyrium made of litharge into the eye.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 The eyes of some men are sometimes born with a red scar covering the pupil, turning it towards the whites and making it resemble a balustrade rose; and the procedure is that the patient places his head over your healthy one, then you open his eyes and pull all that skin towards suitable hooks, holding it with force. Then cut off the first skin and continue cutting smoothly until the end, taking care not to wound the eye in the process. Use a scalpel as we described in the incision of the nail and small forces used to remove a splinter, as shown in the following form after this chapter. And when the incision is complete and all the skin is removed, apply a mixture of rose collyrium or similar corrosive medicines to the eye, then place cotton with egg white yolk over it, ensuring that it is protected from hot abscesses. If anything remains and the pus begins to overflow, suspecting a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with soothing remedies until it heals. Then return to your work once it has healed, following this method for each layer of skin attached to the eye in such a way.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is important to lighten the treatment of each weak eye by natural means and for accidental causes with surgery; and do not rush into any of these procedures before you see that this limb can withstand the procedure.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 Certain are red veins that are located above the eye and hinder the vision's function and weaken the eye all days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 It is necessary, therefore, that you first examine whether the eye, in which the swelling is, is outside [the socket], and if there is no other disease but the swelling; then treat the eye in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head in your lap, then carefully pull the edges of the wound all the way around according to your skill, and let the edges be fine double folds in this shape.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two incisions by degrees in one body in this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully extract those veins and wipe the blood away hour by hour until you see the red veins moving outside of the eye; and be careful not to poke the eye with the tip of the spatula, and perform this procedure at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not cut more than the veins; and when you have done this, instill a mixture of green and red bile into the eye to dissolve any remaining sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to extract all of it in that hour, make a plaster for the eye with calming ingredients to alleviate eye pain and leave it on for several days until the pain subsides and any risk of infection has passed; then continue with the previous method until the eye is healed. This is the shape of the forces (treatment):
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The experts call a fistula of the eye an "arissati": when you cure it by cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a trick to it: you need to make an incision on the abscess, where it should burst, and drain all the pus that is in it until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then take all the instruments that I have described; and it is called an "aspre chief", and should be made of iron in the shape of a rounded head, and sharpened like a file as shown in the following form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the "aspre chief" on the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers and press down firmly until you feel that the corruption has been removed; do this several times, then restore the layer of drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the wound is closed and flesh has grown, and the body of the boil is closed, and it remains so for 40 days without becoming inflamed or developing abscesses, and no other adverse events occur, know that it is healed; unless, there is no other means but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose in this manner: reveal the bone a second time by using a hot iron and medical drugs, and when it has been revealed, take a gimlet of this shape, and let the gimlet have three angles, and let the handle be made thin up to the tip as you can see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 then place it next to the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye pupil, then turn the entire style until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through a sensation of wind escaping if they hold their hand over their nose; and then restore the site with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens, the matter will go to the nose; making it an easier task for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye socket.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is open wide and there is no disturbance or decrease in vision, then bind the patient, then cleanse it, then apply suction cups or leeches without striking, then place a bandage made of vinegar, aloe, incense, and sarcocola on the eye, and then strain the eye and dress it with compresses and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is to take soft cloths, folded in four layers, and then place one upon the other according to the quantity needed for the eye; then bind it tightly with a sturdy bandage, and reapply the suction cups without striking; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the bandage weakens, strain it very much; then remove the bandage after a day and night, and if you see the eye improving, that is good; if not, continue with the dressing and cloths and bandage until it has healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of a detached retina.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the grown-together flesh, it becomes visible and comes out like a piece of resin from paper; then, if you see such a sight, the procedure is as follows: insert a needle into the root of the lower part all the way to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the eyelid; make it go through and leave the first needle in place according to its position. Then cut the loose end of the double thread and tie one end of the eyelid around it, pulling it tight, then remove the needle and place a wet linen cloth soaked in egg yolk on it. Leave it until the thread dries out with the eye, then cure the eye with comforting remedies until the wound heals; and sometimes the wound is kept closed by the eyelid on both sides of a circle of fabric until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has a serious appearance, pierce it gently with a thin stylet that comes from deep within the eye, and let the watery humor come out and let the eyelid droop and enter inward; then extract it until it heals.
de la bowe de l’oil	Here's the corrected translation:
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but a bubble that forms in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water; and the appearance of the work is such that you should have the patient sit on a prepared seat with their back straight, then take their head in your hands from both sides, and turn it until you see the bubble come above to your eyes; then let it become fixed and let the light not descend or be obstructed, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bubble is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 if you seat the patient between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make an incision on the horned veil up to the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horned veil and the cornea, so that the pus comes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that has been boiled and mixed with honey, then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters (or fluids) of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have similarities of waters in the division, and that which is necessary for piercing; we operate accordingly based on health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from light for the sun, and cover the healthy eye very tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the cornea by the thickness of a hair in the corner of the eye at the lower tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" vigorously and turn your hand until it pierces the corner of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary for the measure of the way of almagda to be at the bottom of the measurement of the distance from the pupil to the end of the darkness; and this is the cornea of the eye; and you will see the bone in the paper by the clarity of the horned veil, and then place the instrument until it reaches the place where the water is, then press it down one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 if the water recedes now, the patient will see in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After a short rest, and if the water rises again in the second vein, apply force with the instrument, and when it is stuck and no longer rises, gently extract the maggot while turning your hand slightly; then put a little bit of gemstone saltwater into it, and raise the eye from this.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then put in front of the eye wadding or wet wool soaked in rose oil and egg yolk, and bind it with the healthy eye.[Notes: The text seems to be describing a procedure for treating an injured eye, possibly involving cauterization (heat) or extraction of foreign objects. It also references various medical techniques such as incision, evacuation of blood, and setting bones.]
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, put on a common broth with an abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for some men have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 Therefore, perforate only the conjunctiva and not too deeply, but make the opening subtle, then apply almagra as we have said; and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient a comfortable sleeping area, where they may sleep on their back in a darkened room; and be devoid of all movements, and partake of light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and keep him bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in that same darkened room, and test his vision, and have him look at certain things, and then replace the binding until the seventh day; and it is not appropriate to perform this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but you should lighten it, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 if abscesses are about to come, let him unbind the eye before the seventh day, and direct it towards the side that eases abscess; and when it has calmed down, let him unbind the vision and place a compress on its face to cover for some days, and let him always remain in that darkened room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then go out of the house little by little and return to your duties; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And a man came to us who was from Ireland, who told us that in their country they make styptic by piercing, from which one sucks the water, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor do I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the shapes of styptic, because those who do not know them may see it; and they should be made of pure copper:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let their heads be of this same delicateness, and their tails in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from (the) nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes various kinds of swellings or lumps appear, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such ones that have hardened flesh of a fox-colored hue, and also soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Then in the case of such a wound that is mild and not inflamed, you should make the patient sit between your hands with their face towards the sun; clear their nostrils, and apply a probe to those wounds, and pull out any pus; then collect as much as you can hold in the delicate, sharp spatula on one side, until you are certain that the wound is completely cleaned.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be cut, open it with a very fine and light instrument so that nothing remains; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if they are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them until the blood stops and all of the flesh is removed, then pour vinegar or water on the nose.[Source language: Old French]
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If the nostril does not clear and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; but if moisture does not drain as it should, know that there is pus stuck to the bone above, which the instruments cannot cut; in this case, you should insert a fairly thick linen thread, loosely tied at regular intervals of about an inch or less; place the end of the thread in the patient's nose, and pull gently while sniffing until it comes out of the nose into the mouth; children often do this in school, and it is an easy thing to do for those who want to do it; then hold the part that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other part that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and feel the knots carefully.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Perform this procedure so that you know the wound has corrupted the flesh, then pull out the sutures, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all remaining flesh; and then place a splint of wood on the nose for several days until it is healed, and if drying medicines are needed, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, which distills oils and medicines into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or brass, similar to an open lamp, such as a funnel, and the spout the same; and if you wish, make a closed funnel, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from (the) nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a sickness arises in the head of the nose that is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large at times, to the point where it is visible; and therefore, you should cut it at the beginning and remove it completely, then place the cautery or hot medicine on it; and if you wait until it has grown large before cutting it, see if it is hard, of a purple color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when cut even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of purple color, and you see that you can remove it completely, then empty the patient and cut it carefully without fear, and cure the area with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilaginous works, it does little good, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two edges together with a stitch, then cure it until it heals; and if the edges are separated on one side and the other, then you must cauterize all the parts of their flesh until they heal, then bring the two edges together with a stitch, and bind it, and put powder of dragon's blood, and crushed incense on top of the powders, and place a piece of strong plaster or another healing plaster on top of it, and leave it until it sticks to it, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is to align the edges: either with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
