A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To some men there come within the lips hard abscesses like peas, sometimes smaller and sometimes larger; then you must turn the lips, and make an incision in each nodule, and take it with forceps and cut each part; then apply the place after the incision with powdered vitriol until the blood stops flowing; and then leave it open to air, and cure the place of dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a swollen flesh arises on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with forceps and cut at its root, letting the pus or blood flow; then put vitriol powder or other restraining and desiccating powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, you should cut it again and cauterize it; for it will not come back after cauterization. And these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of abscesses or swellings
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, scabs that are ugly and rough appear on the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, greenish, or gray, indicating corruption reaching the gum, causing the teeth to stink; in this case, you should make the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and scrape off the visible parts of the affected teeth and scabs until nothing remains; and similarly for blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, continuing until they are clean. And if you remove what appears to be loose at first, that is good; if not, repeat the process on the second and third days until everything has been removed. Be aware that teeth require various shapes of instruments for scraping depending on the work required, as the scrapers used between the teeth have different forms from those used for the front surfaces of the teeth; and be sure to have all necessary forms prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat a toothache, you should delay drilling as much as possible, for it is not something to be done hastily, as the substance of the tooth is very valuable until there is no other option for relieving pain.[REGENERATIVE MEDICINE: AN OVERVIEW](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2676341/)Regenerative medicine is a branch of translational research in tissue engineering and molecular biology which deals with the process of replacing, engineering or regenerating human cells, tissues or organs to restore or establish normal function. This field holds the promise of regenerating damaged tissues and organs in the body by replacing damaged tissue or lost cells due to disease, injury or congenital defects. This field is closely related to tissue engineering and molecular biology as well as stem cell research.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then, when the patient is about to pull, you should make sure that the tooth loosening tool is ready.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Often, the pain deceives the patient, and they believe it is in a good tooth, and they have that tooth pulled; yet the pain does not go away, until the bad root is removed, as we have already seen with certain surgeons; and when you are certain of the loose tooth, you must cauterize around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gum all around; then, use your hands or fine pliers to gently rock the tooth back and forth until it is loosened, then firmly secure the pliers; and have the patient's head rest between your knees, holding it tightly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extract the tooth without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and gently insert it on each side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, you must fill it with cloth where the holes are; and hold it delicately with pincers, so as not to break it when holding; and you must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take care not to break it, and leave a part of it, for if the root remains, it will cause greater pains to the patient when it comes back.[NOTE: This translation is based on the context provided in the previous lines, where the tooth needs to be extracted. The phrase "reveigne au malaide" suggests that an attempt to extract the tooth was not successful and some part of it remains.]
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And take heed that you do not act as some ignorant surgeons do, who in their haste and recklessness sometimes break the cautery, and do not bring about what we have described; but instead sometimes bring about great harm to the roots that remain, or by breaking the cautery, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs there, which often happens, use vitriol powder; and if that is not effective, cauterize the area.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used to pull teeth first should have long and thick handles that do not bend when pulling the tooth. Here are the forms (shapes):
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick size so that they do not bend when pulled, and let them be made of good iron, and let them have teeth to hold on to wounds.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains after pulling (the tooth), you should place a piece of cotton soaked in butter on the area for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 as long as the place is softened, then put on the pliers which are called "algefri", making the head appear like a bird's beak; and have them made inside with a file-like shape, and this is the method:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all those tongs, you must cut open the flesh all around the root, and place in it the instrument called "althali", that is, a scalpel, of this shape:[Notes](Note: The above translations are based on my best interpretation of the Old French text provided. I am not a professional translator, so there may be some errors or nuances that I have missed. Additionally, medical terminology in the 12th-13th centuries is quite different from modern medical terminology, so some terms may be difficult to translate accurately.)
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break easily, and if the root jumps out with this, that is good; if not, use all the instruments, whose shapes are shown below:[Notes](Note: The above translations are based on my best interpretation of the Old French text provided. I am not a professional translator, so there may be some errors or nuances that I have missed. Additionally, medical terminology in the 12th-13th centuries is quite different from modern medical terminology, so some terms may be difficult to translate accurately.)
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one helps oneself with this tool which has two handles, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments which are in front of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these tools be strong enough that they cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and likewise other tools which are not mentioned here; and the wise master subtly finds his own tool according to what his work and the illness reveals, because there are such diseases for which the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity; and one breaks neither the cartilage nor other bones, or it will rot, so one searches among the tools that are needed, as I have said, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and sturdy enough to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but rather holds and removes it; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines for this purpose, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, use this entire tool to scrape it away:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and the same is true for young women, you should determine if the tooth is not erupted after it should have, and it is not in the correct position, and it cannot be straightened or filed: then file it down; but if it is protruding over the other tooth, take this instrument with the shape shown here, similar to a small beak, and made of sharp iron, and...
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And place the muzzle on the mouth and keep it there for several days due to the tooth's hardness, so that you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that it can be filed down, file it with a file such as this one shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like the file used to make needles; and file down the tooth lightly for several days so that it does not move until it heals; then use a flat instrument at the end, similar to a razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth come in or grow in. The word "lochent" is the present tense of the verb "locher", which means to come out, sprout, or break through (as in the case of teeth). So, "quant li dent lochent" can be translated as:
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the front teeth become loose, either from being knocked or from falling, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without it falling out, and curing with constricting medicines has not worked; then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the wire and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the loose tooth between the remaining teeth, whether there is one or more than one, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again from where you started, and gently and snugly tighten your hand until it no longer moves; and let the wire be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then bind the jaws with a thread using pliers, and align them, and place it between the healthy tooth and the loose one, and position it so that it does not cut the tongue; and keep it tight as long as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the threads break, then tie it with another thread; and let it remain and serve in this way all its time, and this is the form of teeth and the shape of aligning two healthy teeth and two crooked ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place as soon as possible, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and skilled meddle with it; and sometimes the shape of a bone from an animal is made, and it is placed in the gap where it is needed, and it is constricted as we have said, and it stays and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tie of the tongue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes there is a ligament beneath the tongue or naturally present at birth, or due to an accidental closure of a wound; and the procedure is as follows: you open the mouth of the patient, hold their head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide enough that the tongue is loosened from its base, and if there is hardness or knot, which is due to a healed wound, insert the hook and cut the ligament wide; and make sure not to cut too deep, so as not to injure the artery below; and when you have finished, apply a compress of rose water and ease, or cold water, then place a linen bandage under the tongue; and have the patient change it every night, so that the ligament does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if bleeding occurs, put vitriol powder on the wound; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize it with a ligature cautery, which is good for that; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a bluish-black or hard color, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, then throw the "oncine" (a type of medical instrument) and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood comes to meet your work, then apply vinegar powder until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift the limb easily and gently, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes abscesses called "godath" come inside the throat, which are properly called the two almonds (tonsils). And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is hard abscesses of little sensitivity and a bluish color, do not touch them at all with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them at all with iron, to avoid bleeding; but leave it alone until it softens, and then you can remove it, or it will break by itself; and if it has a whitish color and fine roots, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first check whether the hard abscess is calm and pacified.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit down in front of the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and have him open his mouth and take the surgeon's instrument between his teeth, and press his tongue down with all the instrument, like this is the procedure; and it should be made of silver or fine brass just like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And when you press the tongue down with this entire instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the "oncine" (a type of medical instrument) and stick it in the almond (swollen lymph node), and draw it out as much as you can; and draw some of the pus with it, then cover it with the instrument, of which this is the method, that resembles forceps; and yet the jaws are curved, one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument at hand, take tongs instead, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let one side be sharp and the other blunt; and once you have closed one of the almonds (lobes of the tonsils), close the other in the same manner, and after the incision, rinse the patient's throat with warm water, or water and vinegar, and if there is bleeding, rinse the patient's throat with water, or the skins of pomegranates cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then treat it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses form in the throat besides the two almonds (lobes of the tonsils), so cut them out in the same way as the two almonds (lobes of the tonsils).
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say, a small abscess; and she had tightly closed her entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the passage that was blocked, and she could not eat or drink, and she would have died if she had remained in this state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess had grown so much that it had protruded two grains through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I hastened then and quickly inserted one probe into one of the nostrils, then pulled it out with a large piece of pus; then I put another probe into the other nostril and held her mouth open and pressed on her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses and cut off a portion, and only a little blood came out; and thus, the passageway in the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut away at this abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing, and filled up the space that I had emptied, so that it became very large; then I tied it off and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it ceased to grow; and I left those parts, not knowing what God did with her after I left.
de l’uve	of the eye (eye-related)
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is beneath, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, and you see that the chief abscess has calmed down and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and the one that is round assembled and is not long; and it is blood-red or of a fawn color or black, then you must avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it according to the manner that I have said, regarding its swelling and length, you must make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye and pull it down, and cut it at one of the two points that I have mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.[Brainsize\_1B]: Thank you for your help! Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you do not cover up the excess that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cover up more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being covered (during the procedure), you should use strategy to cauterize him without causing fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the method of cautery is with sharp pointed iron.[*](aigu means sharp in old french)
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient should place his head in your hands, and then press his tongue to the instrument that we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and moisten it with live steam so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the tip of this instrument, the shape of which is as follows:[Note: The rest of the text describes the shape of the instrument used for cauterization]
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let there be a hair or something to hold the medicine, such as the handles of a spoon, and place the instrument on top of all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie down on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and cause choking. Then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye, for a quarter of an hour, until you see it reddened and the bites of the medicine are calmed down; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with the cotton into the wound above, until the cotton hardens on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is finished, then let it dry, and it will fall off after 3 or 5 days. And if you need to restart the cauterization of the medicine, then restart it, and after the cautery, wrap the area around the eye with cotton stuffed with butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take hyssop and rosemary and oregano and rue and chamomile and elderberry and similar herbs, and mix them all together in one pot, and add water, and bring to a boil. And let the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And let it be of silver or bronze, and let one of the pieces be placed in the patient's mouth until the vapor reaches the eye through the optic nerve, until the eye is mortified; then restart it frequently, until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it except at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this instrument is not present, take a small stick and put an eggshell in the patient's head, so that their mouth is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to irritate the mouth, and it is a good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often, a bone or fish spine, or any other object gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press the patient's tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what is not visible to you and has lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit, when the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of cloth, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of reed in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it may enter the throat more easily and keep the head raised up; and take care not to touch the epiglottis or choke the patient, nor push the bone in further; and it is better if the patient inserts the instrument themselves, so they can feel where the object is located; whether they push it down, or pull it out completely with the instrument, until it is removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the vein is medicated, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then look at the patient's throat in the sun, after you press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the vein, then draw it out with a small hook or delicate tongs that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that is not helpful, then take a boiled cane and insert it into the patient's throat, then apply a hot iron to the movement of the cane, and do this frequently.[Note: This treatment seems very dangerous and should not be attempted. It is important to consult with a qualified medical professional for any health concerns.]
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And the patient will be feverish all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in, swallowing none of it, and move it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the swelling senses the water, it will drop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not drop as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will drop without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And the method of fumigation is as follows: take a pot with live coals in it, and cover it with a perforated cloth, with the opening of the instrument placed in the hole; then apply your fumigation and have the patient place the end of the cane in his mouth, closing it so that the smoke does not escape but reaches the swelling. The swelling will now drop, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation many times. Allow the patient to experience thirst, and give him salty foods, but do not give him water. And then it will be necessary for it to come out by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one pulls the vein, it is, when it can be seen, similar to bent pliers so as to easily enter the throat; and resembles a surgeon's beak, and has roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many kinds of abscesses there are, according to what the memory brings forth hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and it is in two ways: one is in its very likeness, and those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is according to the locations where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For abscesses of the head are different from those of the belly, and abscesses in fleshy parts are different from those that come in joints, and each one must be judged accordingly in treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And there are abscesses that should not be lanced until the boil is ripe according to its maturation; and there are such as must be lanced when they have grown, and do not mature according to their development, such as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when abscesses come near joints, and are left until they rot around it, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 Or if the abscess is near the main member, and you delay the incision until it has decayed, it will harm the main member; or it is near the foundation, then one should pierce it so that it decays; and one must not pierce an abscess that is festering without digestion being completed, except for one that is near the foundation, so that it does not rot inside and become elongated, causing a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is mature according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the lessening of the fever, and the diminishing of the pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in the place where it is most dependent on the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and at nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no crease.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bend, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to leave the puncture until it is firm in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it before this, the body of the pus will be prolonged, and it will be full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is an abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.[
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses, small holes; and for large abscesses, large holes, and many cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core, and cover it; when it has become as a cloth, and is deadened, one must do similarly as for boils: and if there are such that are cut in three angles, and if there are such that are cut as the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of glands; and if there are such where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Those who have no head, such as a soft surface abscess, it is necessary to fully pierce it; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and has collected a great deal of pus, and you pierce it, do not pull out all the pus in that hour, but pull out some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then pull out some more; do this many times, little by little, until all the pus comes out; do the same even if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman, or small children, or old decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit (gas) sometimes jumps with the evacuation of pus, which may cause the death of the patient, and you would not be aware.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have lanced your abscess, clean the wound and check if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a shallow cut, apply linen or old cotton bandages; and if it is large abscesses with many holes, then you should put a tent in each one so that they come together; and if you have cut off a piece of skin on the abscess and pulled it aside, you should fill it with old cotton or linen rag without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and dress the wound with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, bring cold and fresh water, wet a cloth, and apply it to the wound many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, apply remedies and care, and use the powders that I have mentioned in light tension in this book, and if it is during winter, and the place where the abscess is is very tense, then you should put up tents and wet cloths in hot wine and oil; and if it is in summer, and the place is fleshy, then you should place wet cloths in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess and dry and treat it, as is appropriate, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what must be universally understood in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	The word "des soros" in Old French refers to swellings or tumors. It can be translated into English as "abscesses" or "swellings". In modern medical terminology, it could refer to a variety of conditions such as cysts, boils, abscesses, or other soft tissue masses.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where small abscesses come out on the skull, and they are of a type that are in networks, like the wattle of a chicken, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 Some of them are fatty and similar to those that contain moisture like pustules; and there are some that are hard and stony when cut into, with no doubt that the artery opposes it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of cutting involves testing each instrument called "entromissoire" to determine its contents and shape.[Comment: The term "entromissoire" likely refers to a surgical instrument used for making incisions or probing wounds.]
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 For if it contains moisture, they open it from the top lengthwise.[Comment: The text suggests that if the "entromissoire" instrument contains fluid or pus, it should be opened from the top lengthwise, perhaps for drainage or examination of its contents.][Continued in next message due to character limit.]
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is evacuated, skin it without leaving any of the skin that contains the moisture, for it comes back if anything is left; then soak a cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those staying overnight will take care of it.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then repeat the process with a cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are certain that none remains overnight; then clean the wound with appropriate ointment, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess contains pus, cut it in length as follows; and insert your fingers, and skin it all around, and make sure to drain all the pus; and if an artery opposes you, do what I told you before.[Note: The text does not specify what the speaker had said before about dealing with opposing arteries. It is assumed that this information was provided earlier in the text.]
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And similarly for the abscess if it is hard, and to cut and to cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cutting into a hard and moist abscess is easier, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if there are some abscesses in which there is no moisture, such as those I have seen on the head of an old woman; and the abscess was like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if one had struck it with something, it would have caused a wound just like from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 And in other abscesses appearing on the head, except for those that appear on children's heads and at the roots of ears, the incision should always be made at the lowest point so that pus can easily drain out; and cure them as is appropriate.
des scrophules	The term "scrophules" refers to a type of abscess or swollen lymph node, typically found in the neck. The name comes from the Greek word "skirphere", meaning "hard tubercle". Scrofula is often associated with tuberculosis infection and was commonly referred to as the "King's Evil" in medieval Europe, where it was believed that the touch of a monarch could cure the disease. However, this belief has been proven to be false and scrofula is now treated with antibiotics and other medical interventions.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Many times, these abscesses occur on the neck, and below the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and are large, and are connected one to another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each individual "scrofula" (a type of swollen lymph node) is specifically located in its own region, just like the nodule and abscess on the head, as we have said; and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and there are some harmful ones that do not want to obey health (meaning they do not respond to treatment).
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In that case, when you see one that is well-disposed to the touch, and has the same color as the skin, and moves from every side and is not swollen on the nerves of the neck or on the artery or vein, and it is not deep; then you should cut it open from above, and remove the covering from each part, and spread the two lips of the wound with sutures if necessary, as we have said for abscesses on the head. And press and press (to drain), and be careful not to cut the nerve or vein, and make sure that the scalpel is not too sharp or cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and do not go too deep, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or any powders that stop bleeding, and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscess subsides, and the wound softens and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work until you have completed it; then examine with your skill if any small scrofulous eruptions remain, cut them and clean (the wound).
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous eruption, it is not appropriate to cut this eruption at its root, but rather tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it.[`samantha_adams`](https://www.linkedin.com/in/samantha-adams-67208b135/)
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut out the entire scrofulous sore, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew it up, since there is no remaining superfluous tissue due to the size of the sore.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you aim to cut out the root of it and pull it out, and then sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For those scrofulous sores that have extra tissue, lance it where it is clearly bulging; and lance it in the same way as previously described, by making an incision and then applying dressings with ointment and similar things, so that it expels any remaining pus; and once the wound is thoroughly cleaned, treat it with a drawing ointment until the skin is healed.
de squinance	The word "de squinance" in Old French can be translated to "of sciatica" in English. Sciatica is a condition that causes pain in the lower back and hips, often due to pressure on the sciatic nerve.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient people spoke and wrote about the operation of the throat (i.e. tracheotomy), but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it; it is only written in their texts.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the divider of the throat called "epiglote" be loosened; and this is not done with the help of anyone, because all the veins and the windpipe of the patient are closed to those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two amandres.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid suffocation which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Then, when we wish to split the epiglottis, it should be split below three or four circles, making a small slit across, between the two circles or according to the length of the slit in the syphac, not in the cartilage; and these places are suitable for splitting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and large.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat completely, then split the windpipe until it reaches the hyoid bone; avoid cutting the blood vessels, if you see anything; and then cut the syphac as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the trachea which jumps out through the ruptured opening, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed during which there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the throat and sew it up all the way to the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh until it has healed completely.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and the breath fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then place a bandage on the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are kept from dying; and for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it passes in 3 or 4 days. And then they command to sew up the wound and cure it, until it is healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a young woman took a knife and plunged it into her throat, cutting part of the muscles in her neck; and I was called to cure her, and found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had flowed from it, and I knew for certain that she had not opened a vein or directed it away from her throat, and the wind was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried and sewed up the wound, curing it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the young woman except that she became hoarse of voice, and later returned to her normal state; therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis, one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 These abscesses are called "goiter hernia," and are large abscesses in the color of a lump, and are very common in women; and is according to two ways: natural and accidental; where the natural one has no malice.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accident is according to two ways, one of which resembles fat, and the other way resembles an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it should not at all be operated on with fire except in the one that is small, and prove and search the entire introitus: if you find it like ordinary fat, and it does not respond to any treatment, then cut it as you would cut fat, and pull it out completely if there is any; and search well around, and cure it properly until it heals perfectly.
des nous	of the knots or nodes. The word "nous" in Old French can refer to a knot or node, and is sometimes used in medical texts to describe hardened lumps or swellings in the body. In this context, it may be referring to an abnormal growth or swelling in the body that needs to be treated.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways there are, which I will tell you all the likenesses; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference which is between dislocation and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is heat and fever holding, until the ebullition (boiling) has passed, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With the nose there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains a tumor (I syfac), which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and starts out like a blister and becomes larger; and there are two appearances, either fatty or moist, and very similar in color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the nose, you should first test and inquire about the instrument called "entromissoire," according to its form as described in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the method of inquiry for abscesses of the nose is to take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth, so that you know the instrument has penetrated the bone, according to the size of the abscess; then remove the intrusive object, and be careful that it does not break.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture runs and forms a lump, whatever color it has, then lance it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the incision moisture does not come out, know that it is fat, then make an cross-shaped incision, and take tweezers, and lightly scrape from each side and towards the coat where it lies so that you pull it out whole with the skin; and if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 For if anything remains, the inflammation will return many times; and if some remains, and the blood bothers you, then apply corrosive powder to the wound, bind it up and place something warm on it to soothe the abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the remaining piece is large, then cut the two edges of the wound, and treat what festers in the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the swollen veins are contrary to you or otherwise, hurry and use the vitriol powder, and leave it there for two or three days, until the wound dries out, and let the boiling of the blood subside; then return to cover what remains of the new [incision].
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 See here the forms of invasive instruments, and they are of three types: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are also three types: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses or fistulas; and they are similar to the needles used to sew wounds, and they are made of citrine brass, iron, or silver, and the yellow ones are more valuable, and they are tested with black plumb line for encircling the hollows of fistulas; and there are three types: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of the leeches are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small ones; and there are leeches that have two curves of three types; and there are leeches that have three curves, and they are also of three types; and there are leeches that have two curves, and some with only one curve, and they are of three types; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these [leeches] are sharp, and some only cut on one side, so as to skin the flesh without cutting the vein or nerve; and of those that penetrate, almond-shaped ones are arranged in bunches, so that the patient does not notice their application during the opening of abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one never uses them except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar areas; and sometimes a small instrument, resembling the skin of bladders, is made according to this shape, for stopping blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And they sometimes place it on the wound that bleeds profusely from veins and arteries, and sometimes with this larger shape:[![image](1602978539457.png)](https://i.stack.imgur.com/cCfjr.png)
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes, the nipples of certain men swell when they begin to become corrupted, so much so that they resemble the breasts of a woman; and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, must do so according to the form of this line from b to g.
