puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 then remove the fat and fill the wound with medicine made of crushed flesh, then bring the two lips of the wound together with stitches and cure it until it is healed; and if the nipple points downward and is soft due to its size as it often happens with women, make two incisions above in the shape of two similar splits; so that one is connected to the other at the end of both, such that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from b to g; then remove the skin that is between the two lips and remove the fat, and add what we have said about stitches and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood loss, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it melts the remaining flesh and fat, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are types of hard scrofulous sores or they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Then those who have an excess of moisture should have their hair cut in this manner, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with aged cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply appropriate ointment to it until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofulas, treat it as we have said for scrofulous sores, and if the wound becomes pussy again, apply a cauterization as we have mentioned before.[Translate]
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When an artery is damaged and the skin over it is stuck down, swellings often occur, and the same happens when a vein is inflamed and swollen; this can be recognized when the swelling is long and deep, and when felt with the hands, it feels tight; when it is due to a vein, it is round on the surface and visible; and it is foolish to cut into this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits, ribs, neck, or many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then it is necessary to avoid the iron cure and also the one who is at the head should avoid it, and in the one who is swollen with an artery burst above the skin; then make the incision along the edges, and carefully separate the artery from the webs, until it is uncovered; then place a needle underneath it, and make it pass through to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then point the space that is between the two ties with an intromitter until the blood that is there comes out, and let the abscess be released; then make the cure so that it heals well, until the tie falls; then cure this with appropriate ointment until it is healed; and if the abscess is because of the incision of the vein, then you must stain your hand with what you can of the abscess on all the skin, then place the needle underneath the space that you hold in your hand, and make it pass through, and let there be a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then bind the abscess, as I have told you, with the tie of one of two parts to the two sides of the filament; and if you doubt that the threads will come loose, then place another needle underneath all the abscess on the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four places; then cut the abscess so that the excess comes out, then cut the excess of the skin and leave what is tied; then put a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then make appropriate dressings and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as an abscess can come in the artery and vein, an abscess comes to the nerves when they are wounded or by excessive exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more frequently in the shoulders and hips and all places where there are joints, namely swellings, and its color resembles the color of the skin, and is in various dispositions without pain; and when one strongly constricts it, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but beneath the skin; and it can move in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor downward or upward, and a joint should not be covered with iron: perhaps it would cause contraction; and one that is in the head or forehead makes the skin suppurate.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut into its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a string and flay it, then remove it and stitch the wound closed, and care for it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging abscesses
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes there appear in the belly and not elsewhere "thelul", and it is a disease called "funge" because of its appearance, and it has delicate roots and large lumps; and some are small and others very large; and I saw a man who had two such lumps in his belly that resembled fungi more than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were jagged, and moisture was constantly running from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six; and in making the incision, look and see if the patient is moist, and the color of the "thelul" is white and moist and has fine roots; then cut it with a broad spatula, and have the cautery ready with fire present.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in cutting, there often comes a profuse flow of blood, and if the blood flows too much, hasten then to use the cauterizer; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision of the iron, take a well-made flax thread, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then bind it, and do not cease to bind the flax thread until it cuts the artery, and this without causing pain; and if the roots are thick, there is fear of cutting the same due to the belly, but you can well cut half, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and be careful not to cut the sinew which is of fleshy color and of poor sense and with a lax look.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	Because it is an abscess that has grown worse, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre later in this text.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the swelling comes out.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the swelling comes from a cautery of a wound or crack in the syficus, and is above the belly and in some parts of the groin, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind; and if it is due to the rupture of the syficus and the evacuation of the intestine, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and is a light thing without pain, and open with diverse outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the evacuation of the intestines, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with one's fingers, it protrudes and then returns, and perhaps it becomes constricted, and greatly enlarges at the entrance to the bath and after great exertion.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and opens clearly when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess is large and hard, and becomes fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to wind, it is soft to touch, and the operation is such that you look to see if the appearance is due to the blood of the artery or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 You must let the wound heal.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to the intestines or an abscess, you must instruct the patient to fast and lie on their back with arms extended to the sides. Then, you should carefully tie a bandage around the swelling. Next, command the patient to lie still between your hands, and move around the area indicated by you until all of the pus has come out. Afterward, extend half of the abscess above the ligature with a large forceps. Then, bind it tightly with strong thread or silk cord, leaving one end untied. Perform the operation on the stretched half of the abscess, and insert your index finger to search for the intestine. If you find it caught in the ligature, release it, and push the intestine back into the stomach. If you discover pus, use forceps to remove the excess. If an artery or vein hinders your work, carefully move around it and return to the operation. Insert two needles with strong threads crosswise and pull them through so that they form a cross. Apply pressure to the abscess in four places above the needles. If you see improvement, remove the needles and leave the area to drain and let the dead tissue fall off by itself. Otherwise, cut it away when it becomes thin and rotten. Clean and treat the wound as necessary, and suture the wound closed.
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the similarities of chancre and how one should work on it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that chancre worsens in the groin, and great caution is needed in the cure. And the ancients said that when chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as chancre which is on the breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, it should all be removed when it starts; and when it is large and old, one must not approach it, for I never cured anyone of it before, nor did anyone ever cure it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in a location where it can be removed, as we have said, involves purging the patient of black bile once; then make them bleed if they show clear signs of congestion; then prepare the patient for the procedure by having them empty their bowels. Then cast your leeches or cupping glasses on the chancre and remove all hairs from around it, leaving nothing behind. Allow the blood to flow freely, and carefully clean the area with your hand or some other object. If the bleeding opposes the incision of an artery or vein, cauterize the area until the bleeding stops. Then continue with another treatment until the wound heals.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have previously spoken in the division about the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each type, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only mentioning "eclites"; and one should not touch the iron in these two types: namely, tympanites and hydrothorax, for it is a deadly thing. Therefore, when you treat this type of dropsy with medicines, called "eclites", and the cure does not help, look and see if the patient is weak, or if they have some other illness besides dropsy, such as cough and solution of the belly and similar things; then do not touch it with iron, for there is danger. And if you see the patient to be of strong virtue, and they have no illness but dropsy alone, and they are neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed in this way: lift the patient up straight in your hands, and have the minister press the belly, pushing the water towards the lowest part of the bladder, then take the spatula-like spine according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And let it be pointed, and yet not so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot bleed; then look if the dropsy has spread towards the intestines: if so, you must cut along the belly three fingers' width directly under the navel; and if it is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left side of the belly, three fingers' width; and if it is due to spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to the weak place; then pierce all the way through the skin with the instrument, and insert it, and lift your hand to leave some space between the skin and the abscess as wide as a finger's breadth or more; then pierce the abscess until the instrument reaches the visible place, which is the watery place, then pull it out, and insert this instrument of which the form is described here:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And is similar to a thin silver hook, and is made of light bronze or iron, and has a small hole in its lower part; and on one side, it has three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is cut like a pen's nib, and that is the shape of the incision that writers make with their pens.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 At the top is the aluminum [alemele], so that when the instrument comes into contact with water, it immediately descends on the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, because if you empty more than necessary at that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he will fall unconscious, or he will approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and his pulses; then pull the instrument and retain the water, and it is now retained by the cork that stops the hole above the syphac, which I spoke about, which you pierce in this manner; then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the patient enduring it, and pull a small amount of water; do this for several days, and be careful not to overdo it so that there is only a little water left.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient's condition, and there is a lot of water, then cure it with sepulture or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and have them drink a healing potion; and treat them with drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize the stomach and liver and spleen after the removal of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the blocking of the penis.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Never is a child born who does not have an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 Then it is necessary that he be pierced immediately with a very fine probe according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 then place a thin piece of wood in the opening, and bind and hold it in place for three or four days, and when he wishes to urinate, remove the plug and allow him to do so, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out will not close the opening.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 He whose wound is small, let it be treated with a leaf of plantain, as we have said, and let it be applied broadly.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those who do not have the opening in its place are injured, for some are born with the opening at the head of the penis, which prevents them from urinating unless they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the tip, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the procedure is as follows: have the patient lie down on his back, then stretch out the penis and hold it in a way that the opening is in the middle, like the width of a pen, as it should be. Be careful to avoid any bleeding, which can occur frequently. If it does happen, stop the bleeding using a styptic, and continue treating the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these ulcers occur on the penis, and it is a nasty appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and benign ones; so one should take them with a subtle incision, and cut and clean all (of it), then put wet cotton with Egyptian ointment on it; then cure it with definitive ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the ulcer is malignant, of foul and discharging color, then you should apply cautery to it.[Note: "albathe" likely refers to a type of ulcer or wound, derived from the Arabic word "al-barad", meaning "the leech". The use of cautery in medieval medicine was common for treating various conditions, including ulcers and wounds.]
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cut it, and if the arrow shaft is in so far that part of it is within the skin and part of it outside, then you must first remove the arrow shaft that is within; and when it is separated, cure the part that is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For if you cure it while it is still together, the head of the arrow is not secure and can be pierced, causing discoloration and corruption on its shaft and in the wound; therefore, you must cut away all that is blackened and corrupted, then apply a plaster made of honey, flour, pomegranate rind, and vinegar, and continue to treat it with other cures until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, moderate the moon cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery is useful for two conditions combined: namely, bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you should insert a reed of wood into the penis and make the patient urinate through it; and when the hair at the tip of the penis (which happens to those who have not been circumcised) becomes wet due to wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with an instrument called a scalpel until the ligament is loosened and the head of the penis is freed from all sides; and if it is difficult to do so, then you should scrape it with a spatula-like instrument around the tip of the penis and the foreskin; then gently separate them, and place a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water between them, so that it does not become wet again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the same as the loosening of continuity like other wounds; nonetheless, when we perform this work willingly, and specifically on children, it is necessary that we do the best and easiest work for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision of their children, for they did not practice it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.[I would like to see a translation of this text from Old French into English:
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen that the majority of masters and healers who perform circumcision do so within a day after birth, and with forceps and a single scalpel; they avoid cutting too deep because there are two layers there, and by chance one may cut the upper layer and leave the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the result is that they cut too deep and the pain is doubled, and at the time of cleansing which takes place on the eighth day, the tip of the member is not necessarily healed; and during the cleansing of the nail, by chance the iron may slip and ruin the work, and this happens many times so that it is not necessary to cleanse and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the suturing that is done with thread to the entire wound I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the sutures cut precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you press your hand, cut evenly in the shape of an "I" throughout the entire time; but let the thread be well wrapped around the skin; and the first step in the procedure is to make the child think, if they are aware, that you are only tying the thread around the member, and then make them rejoice in every way possible; then place it straight between your hands, and gather the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the member and blow and pull upwards until the head of the member is inside; then clean it well of the dirt that has accumulated, then bind it with a double thread, then bind it below the hole with another ligature; and hold it for two days by the second ligature at the pocket and thumb index, and cut between the two ligatures, then quickly lift the scalpel and pull the head of the member; then let the pouch corpse run and run, for this is the remedy; and put powder on it and on the powder a wet cloth of half an egg cooked with rose water, infused with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The procedure for purging is as follows: let the two ends be even and sharp, and let them be of equal length as the width of the hand.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purging is when the heart exits through the incision; then you must stretch it to your fingernail, so that the wound forms an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it at your fingernail, hold it with pincers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if three days have passed and what is beneath the penis is swollen, then leave it alone until the abscess has subsided, and gently flay it; cut it as much as you can move it, and be careful near the part of the penis, it will not harm anything.[*Note: I am assuming "verge" here refers to the penis due to the context. However, this word can also mean "rod" or "stick" in Old French.*]
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if you cut too deeply into the heart and it goes beyond, it will not harm; therefore cure it as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	concerning the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The stopping of urine is due to blockage by a stone, congealed blood, pus, charred flesh, or similar things, as we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone located in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should bend on their knees, place their feet on their back, stretch their belly over the back, and restrain the patient's abdomen as much as they can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained for the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe", of which this is the form: and be made of thin and light silver, like the feather of a bird; and let the cane be one palm and a half long, and be fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of urine withdrawal is as follows: take a double thread, and tie to it a bag of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut off the excess wool and push it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on a seat, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil, and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis backwards over the belly; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and have the patient feel it come to the empty place, and this is not done in this order except for the fact that the conduit through which it passes is twisted; then pull the thread along with the entire wool bag, and the urine will follow the wool, then extract it outside, and let the urine flow; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and relieve the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or blood come into the bladder, or there is putrefaction gathered, and you wish to distill waters and medicines into it, then make use of an instrument called a "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see; and the location for inserting the medicine cup should be such that it effectively stops up the urethra without adding anything, so that one can draw out the moisture and insert it when necessary; and when you see fit to inject your medicines into the bladder, place the end of the syringe in the moisture, and pull the plunger; by pulling the plunger, you will draw the moisture into the syringe, and then forcefully push the plunger back in; this way, the moisture will enter, and come to the bladder quickly, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the subtle form of the enema used to irrigate the bladder: here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is made of silver or brass, and the head (noisemaker?) is higher up; and below is the bladder or the intestines fall; then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture which you want to use to cleanse the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a double thread, and heat one end of the moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the male member, then strain your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered, such that the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it roundly around; then insert a strong string through these holes, then gather the circle as one gathers a thimble, and put in it what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do the same as with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division the types of stones and their extraction methods along with medicines; and I have told you the difference between the moved stone in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should work by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is moved in the bladder happens more often in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety; and it appears sandy, and the patient urinates frequently, and then constricts; and there are many of these jumps in the foundation; and the healing is light in children until they reach 4 years old, and is very difficult in the elderly, and is moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the cure, it is necessary to first cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and raise them up, moving him backward so that the stone descends into the depth of the bladder and comes out somewhat; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and let his hands be beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declining downward; then search for and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the area, then hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall by touch alone, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is an adolescent; and insert it into their rectum, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull on its collar; then press with your finger, and push it out where you wish to make the incision.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to lift up the patient's hips with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the hips in the area where the incision will be made; then insert the spatula, which is its shape:[img width=500]https://i.imgur.com/X3Rn6MH.png[/img] (Note: The image shows a modern medical tool called a "vaginal speculum", but it gives an idea of what a "spatula" might have looked like in the medieval period.)
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And make the incision between what is between the hips and the rectum, not in the middle but to the left side of the anus; and hold it straight over the stone, and keep your hands steady, one at the rectum and the other holding the scalpel, and make the incision so that it is wide before and narrow within, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure from the finger in the rectum will cause it to come out without much effort; and know that there are some stones that have angles and sharp edges, which makes them difficult to extract; and some are soft like a grape, round, and easily removed.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Then at that place where there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump out, you should pull with pincers that are like a file at the tip, to extract the stone so that it doesn't shatter; or you insert beneath it a thin curved instrument at the tip; and if you cannot deceive it in this way, then widen the opening a little, and if the flesh is thick, constrict it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, first put in the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut on top, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterward if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, you must saw it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or urine repeatedly comes from the wound that cannot heal; but still try to drain it, or break it up with tongs, as much as you can pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place a damp cloth on it soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then turn the patient over onto their side, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, rinse the wound well with a mixture of oil and water, then apply a dressing of fine-ointment and basilic ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if abscesses or corrosions come in the wound and congealed blood in the bladder, and urine is retained in such a way that it comes out with difficulty: then insert your finger into the wound and extract the blood, for if it remains there, it will corrupt the bladder and rot it; then clean the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help him in all ways you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that every hour that you care for him, you tie his two thighs together and assemble the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the bladder is small, and it is located in the conduit of the rod, and fixed in there, and the urine cannot come out; you can use the treatment that I mentioned earlier, which is to cut it open many times, this excuses you from the need for cutting during this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already tried it in this way.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a fork of iron according to this shape and have three prongs fixed in one stick:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a thread and tie it around the rod below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the probe into the rod until it reaches the stone; and turn the probe with your hand in the stone repeatedly, until you can pierce through the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Is quickly broken, and exits with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any hindering thing, then tie a thread beneath the stone and another above, then place the rod next to the stone between the two ligaments, then pull it out, and untie the tied string, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women (i.e., a woman's kidney or bladder stone)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is passed by women, and if it does occur, the cure is difficult and is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows herself well enough to reveal herself to the midwives, even when she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is often deeper than that of the man, therefore it requires a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessity demands it, then you must take a skillful midwife, and they are hard to find, and if you do not find one, then take a subtle female healer; and present her with a wise pouch in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command from the examination of the stone; and look very well if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the bottom and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she must press it beneath her finger, and command her to insert her finger into the patient's vagina, and seek and press her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, she must move it gently from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, where it is easily accessible, and feel for the stone in that place; and do not move her hand above or below the stone, and let the incision be small at first; then push the arrow into the incision, if you feel the stone increase the size of the wound until the stone can come out; and know that there are many types of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and some have spines.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 if you know the similarities to recognize the dislocation.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the vein swells, apply vitriol powder and hold it in place for an hour until the swelling subsides; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the necessary instruments with you as I have mentioned in removing the stone from men to assist you in your work; and if the vein swells, and it is the artery that is cut, put powder on it and bind it with bandages and bandages, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, for perhaps the patient will die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has calmed down and the place has cooled, return to your work, until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of a carnal hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ranice aquosa is nothing but a collection of moisture or white humor, which is under the skin of the groin and contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the groin between the white humor that we have mentioned; and this does not happen unless a hernia is present.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this ranice is due to weakness in the groin, and this material spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes there is a percussion on the hips, and this moisture has many colors: it is yellowish in color, or without redness, or black, or watery white, and this happens more often; and these are the signs to recognize this gathering, for if it is white like we have said, then it is a ripe abscess, about the size of an egg, and it does not appear that the hips are swollen, because the moisture is all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the very fabric, the abscess is filled with a part of the egg, and for this reason, it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the buttocks and the white membrane, it can be felt well. Therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, examine it with the entire square probe, which its shape is before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows the probe, then judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we cure it with iron, the patient should be bled according to their strength and the fullness of their body; then lay them on their back, on something a little high, and place many bandages beneath them; then sit on their left, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the hip bone; then take the spatula and cut the skin between the buttocks lengthwise down to near the anus, and make your incision straight through the skin of the buttocks up to the white membrane, and carefully remove the skin according to your ability; then pierce the abscess fully with a wide opening, and extract all the water, and then put in your probe, and stretch the abscess upward; and only touch the anus, but not the rod; cut the entire side of it carefully, so that if you do not cut it well, the water will return; and if the egg jumps out during your work, return it to its place when you have completed the incision of the abscess; then sew up the two leaves of the anus with a stitch, then cure it like other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the eye corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie up the vessels that are suspensive, in doubt of bloodletting; then cut the connection to all the suspensive vessels and remove the eye and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if pus has accumulated in two parts together, know that these are two ramifications; cut the other part equally as you have done with the first, then wipe away the blood, and put damp wool soaked in oil of roses into the wound; and put damp wool soaked in wine and oil on top, and place it on the two kidneys, and place folded cloths on top, and bind it all up with a bandage in the shape of this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two cloths, and stuff them with wool as in this shape and sew them together at the groin of the breeches, and let one of the corners reach to the base of the spine, and the other to the side; and let the other two corners be on the two angles, and let all the bandaging be gathered up in the loop of the breeches; and sometimes this ramification is treated with cautery instead of iron cutting, and it consists of taking a scalpel-like cautery, and cut the skin of the kidneys, and heat it as we have said, so that the white pus contained in the abscess is exposed; then take the cautery in this shape, and pierce the abscess with its tip, and peel off the scab with this sharp cautery while it is hot:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And strike in all ways that you can, until you become fully saturated; and take care that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more successful; and move while being careful of blood loss, and be cautious of the procedure of cutting; and if any thing opposes you, whether it be an abscess or blood flow or anything else, then cure what opposes you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to undergo this procedure due to its horror, then perform perforation as I have told you, which is to say when you are certain through the signs that we have mentioned that ramin juice is present, make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in its lower part over its entire width, and place the perforation along the length of the body; and let the hole be wide enough that all liquid may flow out; then put cotton on the surface, and bind it up, allowing the remaining liquid to drain out; then cure the wound until it heals; and if the white cloth does not allow the liquid to exit from the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or instrument used for extracting water from dropsies, the form of which is described above; and enlarge the opening of the wound, knowing that the liquid will return and accumulate after 6 months or thereabouts; and when it has accumulated as before, the patient will pass his days in this manner.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the haunches (or: groins)
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the sectioning of this branch, there is fear in multiple ways, which is why it seems better to let it be; and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	So I say that many abscesses come upon the body, and even upon the haunches/buttocks; and this is due to many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It should be known that it is due to excessive acidic and watery matter, which has spread to the buttocks, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the body; and there is no pain present, and it is a severe abscess; and perhaps it is a hard and fearsome abscess, with a dark purple color, and sometimes it comes from a burst artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is from a burst artery, it is known by the disposition of the abscess being hot when pressed with your hands; and one must not at all touch it.[Again, don't add any comments or contextual information about the text. Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 He who is made for a vein swelling can be recognized by its disposition to the expression of touch of the fingers, and one can easily make an incision based on this likeness, and on the other parts; and it is necessary to cut out the core of the testicles, then stretch the sac upwards, and pull out the white part of the membrane, and free the suspensory ligament from all sides of the sac.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the sac is already hardened with these new characters (growths), then you must therefore extract the sac and cut it out; and if it is adhered to the membrane or in what is inside the vessels, then it is necessary to free all of that attachment and roundly cut it out.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is in that place, you should cut it all away and extract the egg, as we have said.

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the haunches (or: groins)
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess enclosed by a swelling similar to a knot, with the softening of regions, and the patient moves roughly when they walk; and the treatment for this illness is as fearsome as the one described before, but nonetheless we will tell you about its remedy, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.
