ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	not puncturing, so as to hold it with the finger, and pressing gently. And if you wish, cauterize the spine, as described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of an enema.[](Note: I'm assuming that the previous sentence was "Cauterize the spine with a red-hot iron rod, as we have previously described in the chapter on cautery." And the current sentence is a continuation of the previous one, indicating that the shape of the instrument to be used for cauterization should be similar to an enema.)
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes, a enema is made of silver or brass, or melted tin or lead; and sometimes it is made with various sized instruments, depending on who they are prepared for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Then those who are prepared for the care of children and who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small or large enema is as follows: the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And there is a dislocation where the belly is bound, as you see, and the anus within is pierced; and has two openings on one side, and one on the other; and let the belly be used as a pouch for medicines from an animal bladder or parchment, and let it be pierced all around with small holes, and have one digit of space between each hole, then insert a strong thread of hard twisted cord in the holes, and bind the belly as if it were a sack; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer an enema; and this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or similar thing, then insert it gently; then the minister should press it with both hands together until it is all inside, then remove the enema, and raise the patient's legs in the air, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as much as it can; and if he sleeps through the night, it will be a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema to a patient with a disorder of the belly, and the medicine rushes out, then reinserts it until it is stable.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if there are piles or a boil on the fundament, let the enema be as fine as for a child; and this is the shape of the fine enema, where the skin is stretched tight:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division about the care of wounds; now we will tell you about the care of hands and of remedies, according to their implementation.[nos = we (plural)]
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the locations where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are: a blow by a stone, cut by a sword or knife, or by a lance or stick or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound falling on the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, for the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a blow of a stone or similar things, and the skin is torn and the wound is large, and you suspect a hot abscess: then have it cauterized immediately from the same skull if there is little bleeding from the wound, and let the incision be on the opposite side of the injured part; and make the patient empty themselves of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he does not want to be cauterized, let his food be reduced, and let him not drink wine or eat meat or any char; and place on the wound, if a hot abscess is likely to come, cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, but it is fresh and has all its blood and is not moved by air, then put on a powder that I will mention a little later; and if the wound has been moved by pus, then place some poultices until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as from a sword and similar ones, and the lips cannot come together with sutures, then bring them together with stitches, as I will say for wounds of the abdomen, through stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed to the bone, and is deep and only holds together by a little bit, then cut it; next, cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat solid foods, such as heads and roasted barley, also poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find rotten flesh on the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, then cut away all the rotten flesh and discard it, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or a vein, cut it out without hesitation, and if it is loose, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy: and that is to apply this powder which coagulates once the wound has been cleaned.[Read More](https://hellotext.com/blog/medieval-french-text-translation/)
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is as follows: take one part of incense, two parts of dragon's blood, three parts of quicklime, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly so that it dries out thoroughly and joins with all its blood; and then bandage it well, leaving it unbound if it does not swell; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with cauterizing irons only, when incense or dragon's blood is not available, but as long as the surgeon has not yet moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the ulcer has corrupted the wound, then do not apply this powder at all; instead, apply digestive ointments or a poultice of barley flour made with water and honey until it discharges pus; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the fracture of bones comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate forceps; and I will tell you later about skull fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, except when a nerve or artery of the neck is cut.[INTOXICATED = under the influence of poison; INTOXICATION = the condition of being intoxicated]
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerve, there is no other means but to leave the wound alone and not apply anything restricting, for that harms nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be mild, such as lime washed in clean water, and mixed with rose oil, and also the lime washed in clean water, and other similar stones, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, stitch and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.[Comment: "cout" means to sew or stitch; "bendes" means bandages or strips of cloth]
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and swollen and filled with pus, pierce it lower down if needed; and if an artery is cut and bleeding comes out, tie it off, and bind it up, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spines of the throat are cut, or the windpipe, and the passage is kept open so that food can pass, then sew the windpipe to the groove in the throat, and do not touch the throat but rather return it to its natural shape; and then bind it snugly, and leave it for a few days, then cure it with discarded poultices until it is healed; and if the wound has left an impression on the bone, seek it out; and if there are pieces of bone, pull them all out if you can, and those that you cannot, leave until the wound rots, and becomes separated and heals at the edges; and if the wound is fresh, powder upon it the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is also a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.[NOTE: The word "fistula" here refers to an abnormal duct or passage within the body, often between two internal organs or leading from an internal organ to the skin's surface. It can be caused by injury, infection, or disease.]
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound caused by a spear or knife.[NOTE: These two objects are mentioned specifically as examples of sharp weapons that can cause deep and potentially infected wounds.]
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a spear or knife blow, and the wound is deep, look if from the wound an air void arises while the patient is breathing: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at first or bind it tightly, for the blood does not coagulate in depth and returns to the heart, causing quick death to the patient. Instead, apply a drawing ointment and bind it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient rest on the wound for 3 days or 4, or more; this way no spasms, bad tremors of the heart, nor strangulations of breath will occur. And when you see good signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Heal then the abscess and other wounds, until it is healed; and if it cannot be healed, know that there is a fistula; heal it as it should be done.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, whether it is on the belly or back, heal the part in front; if it is large, with sutures; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is close to the bone, and there are pieces of flesh torn off, then clean the wound and remove the pieces; and if they are not separated, then let the wound rot, which will make the extractions easier. And for wounds in other limbs, judgement should be as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small; sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out of a large wound, for which the insertion of them is more difficult, and the suturing is more problematic; and often, a small wound is worse than a large one, because the intestines are harder to put back in place if they are not done continuously; because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, making it more difficult to put them back in place. Therefore, it is better to leave medium wounds open so that the intestines can be returned to their place without difficulty. And you should know that the ruptures of the belly are of four types: the two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the suturing of other wounds of the body and the two other specific sutures are common to other wounds; but they are more particular to the suture of the belly, and I will describe each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestines protrudes, and it is difficult to put back, this can be done in two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in the following way: moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth in lukewarm water, or cook it in a decoction of wormwood, cypress, and pepper, and sprinkle the intestines until the swelling is gone; and sometimes use astringent wine, and it is often effective for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling spread, moisten the inside with vinegar or agrimony that is well cooked, for this eases the opening for a little bit; and if it cannot enter, make an incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut piles; and the first cure is more important than the cutting, that nothing should be cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument to split [it]: cut inside the curve and not through, and see the shape [here].
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged and the inside comes out, put it back in its natural shape and place, if you have the power to do so, for this is better than cutting.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is large, and it is in the lower abdominal area, then you should make the patient lie on their back and place their legs higher than their head. And if it is in the lower abdomen, then you should place the head and chest higher than the injured parts. And likewise, if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, then ensure that the injured part is placed higher than the other. And thus, you should manage what I am saying for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, use what is available to you, then take a compassionate minister who can hold the entire wound with their hand and bring the edges together. This is the common method of suturing, which involves taking a needle or several needles depending on the size of the wound, leaving two spaces from the edge of the wound, inserting a needle with strong thread, and then sewing through the two parts of the skin and fascia underneath it until you reach that part. Bring the two edges of the fascia together in four places, then tie a double strand of thread around the needle in two parts, then bring the two edges of the wound together evenly, leaving two spaces, and insert another needle, then sew with thread as you did with the first needle, and continue doing this as many times as necessary until the entire wound is closed. The needles should be of medium size, neither too fine nor too thick, as very fine needles will cut through all the flesh and very thick needles cannot penetrate properly. Therefore, they should be of medium size. It is important not to insert the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, as this can cause further injury before the wound heals. Once the suturing is complete, clip the ends of the needle so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and apply bandages or cloth around the ends of the needles to keep them in place until the wound heals. This method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds. For a second suture, it is common to bring the two edges of the skin and fascia together using a single needle with medium-sized strong thread. Once you have pierced all four layers, turn the needle back in the direction where you started, as one does when sewing cloth, leaving enough space between each stitch for a finger's width. This method is known to men, and I once sutured a wound on a man's stomach that was over a palm's length long and had intestines protruding two palms' lengths from the wound in the middle of his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I set the intestines back in place after they had been outside for XXIV hours, and the wound was healed by the fifteenth day, and I treated it, and it was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the physicians had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I placed clean old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 I will tell you of the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and insert it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced straight through, place the tip of the siphac or thread where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the inside to the outside; and the technique of this stitch is such that you sew like a pelterer does with furs, leaving a loop of the siphac on one side and taking it up on the other, until the stitching is fully complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second manner of suturing, which Galen properly calls for, is as follows: some people bring two naturally fitting parts together and apply one chief part of the suture to the other chief part in such a way; stick a needle or chief part of the thread close by, and only pierce that spot, leaving the two sides of the wound; then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside in to the inside, to the two sides of the wound; then make both pierce from the outside in to the inside, in two other holes of the thread that are on the other side; and this is the stronger manner of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galen says this word, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, with thread in each; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather; and know that when the rupture is inside the belly, the sewing is more difficult than at other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgment of the wound is as follows, just like the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh, with all its blood, so that the flesh has been moved by the arrow, then replace the intestines and sew up the cut; then put on ground-up dried flesh powder, and if the flesh has been moved by the arrow, put on some available ointment until the wound closes; and tie off the veins, and let the abscess and pus dry up; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you don't have medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to close, old cotton, and move it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 For you do not need any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound might communicate with the principal members, then you should moisten light linen in moderately warm oil, or in rose oil, and place it around the edges and under the buttocks; and if there is pain or corruption in the bowels, and this happens often, then purge them with cold black wine, and similarly if the corruption reaches the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot be healed when it is wounded, and this is due to the multitude of veins that are there, and the subtlety of the entire body, and its similarity in nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the [intestinal] worm exits the wound, put it back in place as you would with the intestine, while it is still fresh; and if it is old and turned black or blue, you should tie off the area that is black, to prevent bleeding since there are veins and arteries there; then cut away the part that is between the tie and let the two ends hang down from the lower part of the wound, to lighten the extraction when the worm falls out, and the wound will swell.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is coiled and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I saw that a man was wounded in the stomach with a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became swollen and developed into a fistula, and both excrement and gas were coming out of it; I treated it as best I could, and did not stop working on it until it had healed and the wound was closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it soldered, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his belly; and he had no pain, but rather improved in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experienced ones said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in such a manner: take a strip with large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the strip has opened its mouth, place it upon the two edges so that it pulls its mouth tight; and then cut off the head, and this holds so that it cannot come undone, then put another strip in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered; and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 The head of this instrument is heated in the interior, and it brings no harm to the patient, and one can bind the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner: take the head of this intestinal filament, which is very dehorned, and then tie the head of this filament to a thin thread of linen, twisted together; then insert the thread into the needle and sew the intestine, and pull it together at the tear; and this method of suture is not outside the path of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no device nor cure, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it matures, is commonly called a "fistula," and the same applies when it breaks open and drains.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And a fistula is, according to its true nature, a hard and white nodule that is not painful, similar in appearance to the feather of a bird; sometimes clear draining, and other times thick; sometimes shallow, and other times deep. I have previously mentioned in the classification of wounds that any wound that has not healed, where there is no flesh, this is not due to anything but one of the Nine causes: namely, due to the small amount of blood or tissue; or due to its malignity; or due to the presence of hard cartilage inside and on the edges, preventing the growth of new flesh; or due to excessive drainage; or due to a putrid location and poor quality matter; or due to improper treatment; or due to corruption being a form of pestilence; or due to slow digestion in the region, resulting in delayed healing and swelling by nature; or there are veins or bones involved. I have already shown all these causes, along with their signs and cures, in the classification.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to make you aware of the treatment of fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that a fistula can happen in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the syphilis, or at the intestines, or at the bladder, or at some of the ribs, or at the spine of the back, or at some joint of the hands or feet; and there are some that come to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all fistulas of this kind are of difficult healing, and there is nothing but effort and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach to the place I mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure, and you recognize it, then take a probe of iron or of steel, if the fistula is straight, then seek it; and if the fistula is twisted, then seek it with a fine probe of wood, for wood bends around the twist; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot seek it well with probes, then irrigate it through one of the holes, for moisture passes from one hole to another, and cleanse it; then seek it skillfully to the best of your ability, so that you know if there is bone or nerve in it, and if it is embedded deeply, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or any of the places I mentioned to you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the abscess and the rotten flesh that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply embedded from end to end, then you must cut deeply, as much as you can, then put in wet bandages with medicine, and push them up to the top of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the remaining superfluity; and then put on ointments that draw healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If vein or nerve does not trouble you, nor the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and discoloration, let the king (surgeon) wait until all corruption is removed, then cure the wound with uninjured flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns crooked as before, know that you have not yet reached the bottom: reveal and search until you are at the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the place; and if it is healed in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it; there is no other means but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone damaged, and you can extract it with pincers, do so with a suitable instrument for this purpose; and if there are many bones, extract all of them, not leaving any behind; and if moisture (pus) opposes you, and there is no mistake or fear, cut through the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place something putrefactive on the wound and leave it until the flesh around the bones has rotted, and then the bones will come apart more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh bone, then merely allow the corruption to subside until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of the corrupted flesh, and it reaches even to the marrow of the bone, then it must be covered and protected until the corruption is healed, and then cure it until it has healed; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help from it in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 A young man of around thirty years old had pain in his leg due to an internal cause that brought matters to the leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no cause for which to operate; but the physicians, out of their foolishness, operated so much on the abscess that it opened, and a lot of matter ran out, and it became a fistula, and a great deal of pus came out that all exited contaminated and moist from the body; and many physicians applied treatment around for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what ran out through the openings was of great size; and the young man's body became red, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I set up a tent in one of these openings, and then examined all the openings, and found that one came toward the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I hurried then, and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the rot came as far as the bone inside; I thought that what appeared to me of the rotten bone was all of it, and I believed there was no other corruption except what I removed; and I began to heal the wound with soaking medicines for a long time, but it would not heal; and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I thought it was all of it, and then I removed it, and took care to heal the place; but I could not do so until I cut around a hand's breadth of the bone, and pulled out all its flesh, then healed it with medicines; and it healed and joined quickly, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For through the evacuation (of blood) he often sweated, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone grew a hard flesh, and it was of good disposition and caused no harm or contrary effect at all, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this way: take a bandage and tie it to the end of the bone that is visible, and command someone to pull it up; and place another woolen bandage, larger than the first one, over the flesh above the bone, and stretch the skin, so as to draw the corrupt flesh underneath, and uncover the flesh above the place where you want to operate, so that the knife does not cut the healthy flesh; and put a piece of wood or a board beneath the bone to cover the corrupt flesh; and it is necessary to operate until one can see and feel the corruption, and operate again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is rotten and not visible, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, reveal all the flesh; then place a piece of ember underneath, and then apply sutures from one side to the other side of the corruption, and let the suture be one finger's breadth away from the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut off the rotten joint, and cover the bone or what it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other option but to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or in the ankle of the foot, this is a very difficult matter, but nonetheless you must examine the corruption, how it appears to you; and clean it in all ways that you can, but not if the vein or nerve hinders you; and know that there are many incisors and sutures for cutting bones, according to their placement, appearance, thickness and fineness, size and smallness, hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each type of work; and know that the task will show you the instrument that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the signs of the types of diseases; so consider the instrument that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The shoulders rot or corrupt either from within or from without; and when you have treated this corruption with the cure of medicines, and it does not improve, then you must cover that member down to the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes from death, or from the greater danger, which is the defect of the member; and the sign is that the member becomes black, so that it seems burnt by fire, and afterward it rots more, since this corruption goes from member to member, taking hold of the whole body; so you must hurry to cover it, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and the like, if the corruption is in the joint of the finger, you should cover it, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it comes as far as the hand, grasp it at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, grasp it with a knife; and if it surpasses the knife, it is deadly, and there is no help beyond the amount of its power; and do thus whenever the corruption comes to a point: if it comes to the first joint, then grasp after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, then grasp the entire foot; and if it rises in the leg, then grasp at the joint of the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means but to let the patient die; and the manner of grasping or sewing the member is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister one of the ties downward, and another minister the other tie upward, and you sever the flesh that is between the two ties to the width of one span, so that the bone is exposed; then grasp or sew, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the suture does not touch the healthy place, and may come to the patient no other lesion or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if bleeding occurs while you are working, then cauterize the area hastily, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the wounded member with a suitable bandage and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in our town: he had a discoloration that looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his foot toe, so that it spread over the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he quickly covered his foot, and it was healed; and long after, the corrosion returned to his hand toe, and he came to me, and I applied reactive substances after the cleansing of the body, but the corrosion could not be stopped; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope to redirect the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because his vitality was weak; and he despaired completely and returned to his land, and covered his hand, and it was healed; and I have only told this story so that others may do likewise, if they are in need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes a abscess forms in the fatty area, and remains so long that it makes a large collection of pus; and then it bursts and pierces, and the pus drains out, leaving the wound open, like a cavity; and the skin that is on top is as thin as delicate fabric, and does not heal up to the bone, nor to the nerve. Such a condition is called "sain", and is not called "fistula". But if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone in depth, it is then called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you cut all around it, and similarly when it is thin, like delicate fabric; and it does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if you believe that the skin has hardened, and corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it with an enema as follows: check if the breast is large, and the swelling that is in it has a foul smell, then enema the patient with Egyptian medicine made thus: take alum, oil, and tar, equally, and put it in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine becomes red and as thick as honey; and then take as much of this as you need, and mix it with water and honey, and give an enema to the breast, and constrict the opening; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then expel it by straining; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed; and sometimes give an enema of water and ashes, when this medicine is not available, and this is done by taking vine ash, and pouring water over it, then filter it, and give an enema with it, until you are certain that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear this, either the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, then give them an enema of water and honey, in which there is a little tar; or give them an enema of honey and wine, in which the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine causes the skin to harden; and when you have done this, and you believe that the breast is well cleansed, then give them an enema made from a substance that causes flesh to grow in it, and this is done by taking diaphoretic plaster, and mixing it with oil and wine; or give them an enema of some medicines and remedies, whose properties I have mentioned in the treatment of remedies; and if the nipple of the breast is small, and the nozzle of the enema cannot enter, then widen it a little with an iron tool, and insert a plug of Egyptian or basilicon ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, then stitch it up and leave enough room for the enema to enter, and if the nipple that emits pus is above, then aim lower down, where the pus is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 For when the wound is deep, it does not let any flesh come through; and if you are unable to cover the wound as you wish, then arrange for the wound to be as low as possible, because when the wound is deep, it does not let any flesh come through and if you are unable to cover the wound as you wish, then arrange in such a way: that the wound runs easily downwards, and lets nothing of the wound escape; and take consolidative medicines to place on the wound, and stretch linen cloth over it that covers the entire wound; then bind tightly around the wound at the lowest point where the breast is more open, apply a gentle ointment on the other cloth according to the size of the wound, and place it on the wound to ease the tension, but do not remove the large cloth outside until after several days once; and the one who is over the wound, often remove it to draw out the pus, whether it be venom or pus or enough or digested or undigested; and keep watch if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature come to the surface of the wound, then know that the breast is already healing and approaching health; and then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change to another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast hangs loose and bloated after many days, know that the breast has not swelled at all.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle venoms linger for a long time, do not lose hope for recovery, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 For there are men who have slow healing of flesh in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if pus does not digest quickly from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healthy; and if the breast is slow to dry and is distant, apply drying medicines in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphoretic ointment, for there is a large part of vitriol in it, and it is the last medicine; take diaphoretic ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and add equal parts of old wine in substance; then cook it and use it; and do the same with thickened honey when diaphoretic ointment is not present, or take myrrh, aloe, and incense, and grind them, and sprinkle the powder on the honey while it is over the fire; and then wrap it in glue and apply a bandage to the breast, and sometimes administer long wormwood and roots of heavenly lily, which is also like vetch flour and centaury; and use simple or compound medicines: grind them and make powder, and put it on the honey that I mentioned, and use it; and if the cure takes a long time and is not cured by this cure, know that corruption has reached deep within, and pressure is exerted on the bone, or on hard members, or on ligaments; then cure it with the cure of fistula as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of an abscess on the fingernail[STH-15]: Here is a possible translation:
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 A panaritium is a abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps in other fingers; and when it has matured, and one does not pay attention, an abscess comes to a head, and they run and spread until they reach the root of the nail, and possibly even beyond; and the decay reaches the bone, so that there is a painful, foul-smelling infection; and the finger becomes swollen and turns purple.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you cure it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not improve, then you must cut away completely with a knife all the remaining tissue from under the nail, and cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and remove it, for as long as corrupt bone is there, it cannot heal; and if you see that the wound is becoming corrupt, cut it in the shape of a "I" as has been previously said, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is punctured and swollen, and causing great pain, you must first cleanse the wound; then cut the toenail obliquely with a knife, taking care that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something soothing on it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the gout in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The dislocations that arise in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there are some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and some of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the knuckles of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one that is born in some knot of the finger does not move, and the one that is born at the joint of the finger, by chance moves; the size of the one that is fleshy is small, in such a way: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: hold him with forceps.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one that is born in the back of the last knot, you must first cut the flesh roundly until you reach the bone, then cut the bone to a thickness suitable for it, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The unions that occur at the hands can come from birth, or from healing of a wound, or from burning with fire, or from similar things.[STT: In those who have unions (fused fingers) at the hands, these can be present from birth, or due to healing of wounds, or from cauterization by fire, or similar causes. ]
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient. Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.
