des vils	 of the common (people)
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 Veins are large vessels full of melancholic superfluities, which come to various members of the body; and it happens more often in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to them purging of bile, and then healing with basilic.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment with iron has two methods: one is to cut it, and let out the black blood; and the other method is that you raise the vein, and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The incision is done in this manner: first, apply very hot water to the leg, until the thick blood becomes thin, then strain the leg of the patient from above the thigh down to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision, then raise and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the vitality of the patient can bear; then bind it up, and instruct him to eat foods that provoke black choler; and begin the evacuation and bleeding again when the veins are full, and this harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The treatment of this is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair, then place them in a bath, and soak the leg in hot water until it turns red and veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire, and then make a cut along the long vein above the head of the calf, or below at the ankle; then pull back the skin with a scalpel, and cut the vein from both sides until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then push the clot under, so that it is raised from the skin, and then gently pull it with the scalpel, then cut in another place three fingers away; then cut back the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it up with a lancet as you did before, and pull it to another hook, as you did first; then make another incision, or more if necessary, then lift it, and pull it to the toe of the foot, then draw and lift it up to the second incision; then pull it out of incision by incision, until it is completely removed, then cut; and if you cannot pull and lift it, insert a strong double-threaded needle, and tie and pull it, and insert it underneath one rail, and turn your hand back and forth, so that it comes out; and be careful not to cut, for if it cuts, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and it will harm the patient; and when you have completely removed it, place wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site; and cure it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the eye socket is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, you should carefully split it open, but do not cut it; and pull it apart as we have previously mentioned.

de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is located in the legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land without moisture. Sometimes it may appear elsewhere, such as on the legs, due to decay beneath the skin that travels between the skin and flesh, like a snake or worm moving within the body.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this ailment are that there comes into the leg a very great inflammation, then the location changes and the vein begins to come out, similar to a plant's root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the incision is made, you should wrap around it a piece of linen that is 3 to 4 fingers wide, and tie it, leaving the linen hanging from the leg. And every time it protrudes too much, you should wrap it again with the linen and tie it; if it is too long, cut off a part but do not cut it at its root until it has fully come out. For if you cut it, it will return to the flesh and cause abscess and putrefaction or inflammation in that place. Therefore, it must be treated carefully and not left in the body; sometimes this vein, when treated, measures 5 palms long, or even 10. And a man came to me once whose measured 10 palms long. When you cut it, insert one finger's width or a hole and pierce it to its depth, so that everything comes out. Let the contents inside be emptied and apply anti-inflammatory medicine for several days, then cure it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein, hands swell, and likewise when it appears at the joint of the foot or leg, and there comes much bruising, and then it subsides; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This illness is called "maladie de buef" (disease of the ox) in our land, because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body going up and down, and one can feel its movement from member to member, until it breaks the skin where it goes, and emerges; and it comes from the putrefaction of certain humors, like worms and snakes and lampreys and ascarids in the belly; and there is fear about its harmfulness, because when it moves through the body, if it reaches the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps it will enter and destroy the eye; and this happens frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you wish to cure and pull it out, one cannot avoid that it goes: therefore, you must then tie the joint firmly above and below with a strong ligament, well tightly; then cut above and pull it out, and if the wound runs deep into the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see it come near the head by the eye, hold tightly beneath it the eyebrow, then cut above and pull it out; and you must have the patient use a cleansing of the body with resolvent medicines for bad humors, and beware of foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain coming from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that appears in certain limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and not long after, I saw it move up to the shoulder, more quickly than any other thing, like quicksilver when it flows from place to place; the pain left that place and settled in the shoulder, and then soon spread throughout her body, until it reached the other arm; she then told me that it would turn around her body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved thus member by member, for I had never seen this disease presented in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues. Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres. des saiettes	 of the arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their shapes and where they lodge in the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The varieties of them (arrows) are such that there are some with large points, and small, and barbed, and barbless; and some that have two wings, and some that have tongues, and some that have pieces; and an arrow that falls in any member falls in two ways: either in a principal member, such as the head, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it (the arrow) falls in any place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear; then one must be careful in extracting this arrow, for death comes after in many dispositions; and when these bad signs do not appear at all, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the dura mater that is above the brain moves, is when there is scotoma (a visual field defect), stiffness, dizziness, and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it exits through the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and there is a flow of moist wound exudate, white like pus, and an escape of brain matter; and if these signs appear to you, then you should refrain from treating it, and pull out the arrow if it is not already in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The signs of an arrow wound when it reaches the heart are: it is close to the left breast, and it feels as if it is stuck in something hard, not hollow; and perhaps the arrow moves like a pulse, and produces black clotted blood, and comes cold sweats and coldness: then know without doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that never bodes well is when there is foam spurting from the wound, and swelling in the throat, and the patient changes color, and sighs heavily and seeks cold air.[](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/porcon)
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls near the covering of the breast, it is next to the ribs; and causes great pain and great sighing and great distress; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow falls into the stomach, it may happen that some undigested food jumps out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow falls into the belly, and dung comes out of the intestines, there is no hope for a cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow falls into the bladder, and urine comes out of the wound and there is strong pain, know that the wound is deadly.[INTRODUCING NEW TOPIC]: Now let's explore a different medieval medical topic - bloodletting. Here's the first sentence to translate:
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms, neck, throat, shoulders, shoulder blades, loins, hips, and legs, are safe according to various conditions.[INTRODUCING NEW TOPIC]: Now let's discuss the medieval medical practice of surgery. Here's the first sentence to translate:
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you about what happened to me so that you can do the same, then do the following:[INTRODUCING NEW TOPIC]: Now let's discuss another medieval medical practice - the use of herbs and plants for healing. Here's the first sentence to translate:
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to a man that an arrow hit him in the temple at the root of the nose: I pulled it out and drew it through the fat of the ear, and it healed without infection.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And extracted an arrow that hit him in the fat of the eye beneath the eyelid, and the arrow was barbed, and I could not reach the point without turning it towards me, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, with a light iron head without ears; the wound healed, and no ill befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And I pulled an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with feathers: I sawed off the beards (of the arrowhead), and carefully pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And I pulled an arrow from a man, who had it fall in his belly, and I thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change. I cut (into) the arrow and levered it out, and pulled it out without any complications.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if you want to treat a man who has an arrow stuck in his back, and the wound has healed over; and the arrow remains inside him, but his natural condition does not change, nor does it cause harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And see another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was healed; and he remained without suffering great pain; and many similar ones.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And I pulled an arrow from a man of the prince's, which had fallen in his nose, and it was slanted towards the right side; and the arrow was fully embedded. I was called to the care after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I searched it with a thin probe and felt nothing; and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.[tnx](Note: The translation assumes that "il" refers to the patient)
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied plaster of attrative and digestive properties to the place so that the place would not swell; and the place of the arrow appeared.[tnx](Note: The translation assumes that "li leus" refers to the location where the arrow is)
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I applied the poultice for many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I placed corrosive medicine on the wound for many days, until it was open, and I probed it and felt the tip of the arrow that protruded; then I applied medicine to the opening of the wound, until the head of the arrow became visible to me; and more than four months had passed when the wound healed so much that I introduced forceps, but they could not exit; then I did not cease to refine and devise various instruments, until one day I took hold of it with well-made forceps, as will be described in the end of this chapter, and I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the surgeons judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I then restore it, and the wound is healed, and the patient is completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the nature of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you may pay attention to what I do not say, for books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters compare well even a small thing, and with regard to what is present and lacking, they find new ways and nine instruments for dealing with unusual things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not exit the members where they are lodged in two ways: either by the way they entered, or from another part; and those that exit at the entrance wound are flesh-wound arrows, which exit sometimes.[](https://www.bing.com/)
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump now, let it be until the flesh is rotted around it, and the abscess is eased; and similarly, if it is embedded in the bone, and it cannot come out, let it be like that for several days, and move it every day; and then it will jump, and if it does not jump, carefully cut around until the entire hole is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is stuck in the skull bone, reaching one of the brain cavities, and any of the symptoms I mentioned appear in the patient: then do not pull it out, but leave it until it is even after several days, because if the arrow reaches the brain cavity, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not stuck only in the bone, and does not reach its target, and the patient remains without any bad accidents for some days, then attempt to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply a styptic around, as I have told you; then cure the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is embedded in the body so that it cannot be seen, search for it throughout the wound; and if you feel it, then pull it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein in the way, then enlarge the wound until it is wide; and pull the arrow out if you can, and if there are ears or anything else keeping it in place, remove the flesh that is attached on both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow so that you do not cause more harm by pulling it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't pull it out in one try, leave it in place until the swelling goes down around it, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood is against you, moderate what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and be cautious of the incision of the nerve and vein, and use tricks on how you can safely pull out the arrow, whether soon or late, firmly or gently; and place the patient in the same condition he was in when the arrow fell to him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place him as the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from another direction, where something is visible of it, or the skin is swollen in that spot if it is seen or felt apparently: then cut there, as much as the pliers can reach, and then pull it out; but be careful now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then rotate your hand circularly until it enters into the bone and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, leave it in, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; and if the arrowhead is stuck in there, push the whole shaft in; and if it is broken, and you see that the patient needs a buttress, administer the instrument beveled, so that the point of the arrow enters the instrument's bevel; and then pull out, and if the arrowhead is stuck, push the instrument with the entering point to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is barbed, it is necessary to cut away all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrow falls in flesh or belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close, and you can cover it, do so; and be careful not to cover the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then stitch the wound if necessary; and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shapes of the forceps used to treat arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and here is their shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.[Note: I translated "quantité" as "size" because in this context it is referring to the physical dimension of the arrow, not its quantity.]
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the arrowhead is similar to a bird's feather, for embedding in the tip of an arrow, as shown in this illustration:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the pliers for putting in and pulling out, as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common bodily veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 Of the veins from which one bleeds, there are thirty-one, of which sixteen are at the head: that is to say, two veins which are behind the ears, called "herbech"; and the two arteries which are in the temples; and the two veins which are on the eyelids of the two eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein which is between the eyebrows; and the vein which is at the tip of the nose; and the two tendons which are in the neck; and the two veins which are in the upper lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the two veins which are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly lanced are five in number: one is the cephalic, located on the left side, which the laypeople call "head vein"; the middle one is called "faste", and it is made up of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the laypeople call it "heart vein"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the laypeople call it "belly vein", and it is above the fascia, and it is the one that is lanced, which is clearly visible on the arm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the "salvatelle" is the vein that is between the ring finger and little finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is located under the fold of the pocket on the left side, and the second is the saphenous vein that is by the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The draining of veins that are behind the ears helps against old catarrh and headaches; and the quality of the drainer, as I tell you, is to raise the patient's head and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a cord until two veins appear behind the ears in two places hanging from the head: then seek them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, stop; then take the lancet and insert it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire length of the vein and cut the skin and the vein well two fingers' width of the incision, and let the blood flow until you see; then bind and tie it tight until it heals; and I have already mentioned the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The bleeding of the two arteries which are in the two temples is worthwhile for old and solid headaches, customary ophthalmia, and watery eyes in the body; and the quality of the bleeding is as I say: and that is that the patient strains their neck, so that the two veins appear openly; and feel the pulse beneath your finger, and then bind above with pressure; then lift the flesh above the vein to the tip of your finger, and insert the lancet underneath, and lift the vein up, and let it bleed, and cover it, as you have done with the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then untie the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on it; and then bind it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their binding and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The bleeding of the frontal vein is worth as much as the bleeding of the cephalic in diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for rheum; and its quality is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the tip on the vein, and strike with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and sometimes the work is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, it is not appropriate for the flame to be too sharp or pointed, and one should not cauterize diagonally because the bone is close, and there is a risk that the cautery may break when it is fine.[Notes:
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The bleeding of the two veins that are in the inner corners of the eyes helps with the eyes, and with lice, and with rheum, and with the orifice in the eye, and with diseases of the face; and the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting with some ligature, as before; then bleed, and let the incision be a little long and wide with the flame, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the incision is fine, it may break; then cauterize the wound to let out blood as needed, and bandage it with cotton, and bind it well.[ST1] \*Note: I am not a medical professional, and this translation should not be used for medical purposes. It's always important to consult with a healthcare provider for any medical concerns or treatments.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The sap of the vein in the nose is worthwhile for headache, and for sudden madness, and for illnesses of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and similarly when it is old; and the qualities of the sap are such that the patient constricts his neck, then constricts his nose with your left hand, and takes a slender flame, and sticks it between the upper lip in the space that is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open widely, and the blood will begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it up for one night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the method of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The scarification of the two sinews helps with the narrowing of the windpipe, and the beginning of consumption, and many diseases, and abscesses, and corrosions, and herpes, and tumors; and the quality of the scarification is such that the patient pulls their neck from under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then carefully open the long vein a little widely, then draw blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then do the same thing in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and gently tighten both veins, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound dries.
de la sainie des leivres	 of the flow of blood (or wound drainage) from the sides/flanks
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Here is a translation of the given sentence:
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of the flow (of blood or wound drainage) are as follows: make the patient sit in front of you and constrict their neck as I have said; then turn up the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the upper lip and the other on the left, and they can be recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the presence of small black veins around them: therefore, stop the flow of both, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, then stop the largest one on each side, and similarly for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of sweat under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The sweating from veins that are under the tongue helps after the sweating of the head, and this is at the narrowing of the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and in diseases of the mouth; and the quality of sweating is such that the patient lies between your hands before the sun, and raises the tongue, and looks down on each side a black vein: then heal one and the other, but do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: either by making a single cut with a broad lancet or a fine, olive-shaped one like cutting scalpels, and it is called "anesil"; and they are broad and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mercurian flame is very famous, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary, for opening veins full of thick blood visible to the eye, and that contain coagulated and turbid blood; and this is the form of the olive-colored flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more finely adjusted, and is for healing fine veins, where there is thin yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The bleeding of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are located below the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed the wound and be cautious of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if he cuts the artery and a flow of blood comes out, it is necessary to stop it, as I have said; and the flame should not be pricking but slicing like a knife.[Answer 4:] The dislocation of a joint may occur due to moisture causing it to move out of place, resulting in a deformed limb and great pain for the patient.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the vein does not open manifestly, you should constrict it, and apply another one; or seek a secondary vein of it, or heal the wound in place of it along the arm: it opens manifestly; and cover it with an escharotic salve, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you wish to recognize the location of the bleeding, you should constrict the arm and touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot with ink, and bind the arm, and cover the vein with an escharotic salve; and be careful not to strike the artery when you see the swollen area, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it bulge up high, similar to a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is from the artery: hasten then, and place your hand on it for a long time, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens; if the arm is swollen, leave it like that and do not move it; and be careful and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and it overpowers you, and the medical supplies are not at hand, then cut the artery if it is visible, for its source retreats, and stop the bleeding.[5](https://wikishards.fandom.com/wiki/Old_French_Translation_Help:Line-by-line_translation#fn:5)
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 Take a piece of fennel bark, split it, and take one half of it and bind it firmly until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and stopping the bleeding is not harmful in many positions for the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's binding.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The wound in the middle helps so that it draws blood from the top of the head and from the body beneath, because it is composed of the basilic vein and the cephalic vein, as we have said; and it is necessary for the surgeon to be cautious about the nerve that is beneath, and if he wounds it too deeply, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the wound becomes infected, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some men due to its delicacy, then you must cure it with a silver instrument; and avoid the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision through its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The wound in the cephalic vein helps so that it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and it is necessary to cure by pricking with the olive-colored flame or the myrtle-colored flame, because it is the safest of all veins, for there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien. La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the lancing (or blood-letting) depends on your judgement.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you need to know about bloodletting is that bloodletting is only performed to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins which are: the cephalic, the fast, and the basilic; and one must perform bloodletting at the beginning of prayers at dawn, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and one must perform bloodletting on the first day or the third day, two or three hours after sunrise.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The dripping of medicine administered for illnesses has no set time, but is rather as needed day or night, at all hours and in every moment; and one should not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying a fetus from the fourth month until seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And one should not bleed elderly people who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when one wishes to be bled, in whatever manner, it is necessary that they empty their bowels with a light enema if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw superfluidities from the intestines causing harm to the principal members; nor should one bleed someone who is overly full of food, or intoxicated, until they are no longer so, nor those who are edematous; and if one wishes to be bled after a colic pain, vomiting, stomach ache, frequent urination in women, work, staying up late, fasting, or any other thing that weakens the strength, whether due to a wound or illness of the body; then refine the humors if the blood is thick by means of food and drink and medicines if you have the power; then enter the bath if nothing prevents it, in order to refine the blood, and bleed from the vein on the side opposite the heart around the third hour, as we have said; and take care on that day to avoid work, exertion, lust, and similar things; and be happy and joyful, and let the one performing the bleeding raise the vessel higher than the person being bled, and rub their arm two or three times, then loosen the ligature gently, for when it is too tight or narrow, the blood cannot flow; and then rub the area around the vein with your hands until the veins swell and become noticeable; then moisten the bandage with a little oil, then place your left hand on the vein below where you wish to bleed, so that the vein does not move or slip away when struck by the lancet.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 Because there are veins that run like strings in the leg, and some of them are filled with airiness, such that when one applies fire, they contract and cannot open the vein. And if the wound is swollen and the patient is frightened, let it be for a day or two and do not bind the arm: perhaps abscesses will come. Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the place swollen, do not restart the bleeding, but instead put a little bit of oil residue on it, for it lightens the body from blood, and the oil residue is adhesive in this place; and thus administer the oil residue in every bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the course of the blood; and do the same with a triacle and poultice of them, when applied to the place; spreading the blood and dispersing it when it is too thick.

For there is much blood inside the body which is already heated and brings on fever; so one must draw off a large quantity, and widen the opening until it reaches the bone; then you should check all the conditions of fracture, and place your hand on the pulse when it bleeds, to prevent death in its place, and this happens many times when the one treating is negligent; and it is not at all necessary, when you see the arm released and causing blood to come out a second time, with the opening closed, that you press hard; nor if it is curved, that he quickly extend his arm, for that would be harmful; but let him wait until it bleeds a second time; or place the tip of the flame there until the clotted blood at the opening of the vein comes out, and put a piece of cloth soaked in water on top, and press lightly.

Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies. des sainies de ventouse	 "of the wound suction cups" or "of the treatment with cupping glasses" (des = of the; sainies = suction cups, from the verb "sainer" which means to heal by bloodletting; ventouse = cupping glass)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this suction cup therapy, which is done without incisions, is of two kinds: one is with heat, and the other is without heat; and suction cup therapy that is performed by making incisions and extracting blood is done in fourteen parts of the body, one of which is on the head; another is on the neck; two others are on each side of the collarbone; one is under the chin; another is on each shoulder; another is on the hips; another is between each arm; another is on each leg; and another is on each ankle; and this suction cup therapy does not draw large amounts of blood, only small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken the body as much as bloodletting; and it should not be administered, either with or without heat, in any illness caused by excess until the whole body has been emptied.
