Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, lift the leg with ease and then with water, very gently, and then wrap it up; and if the wound takes too long to heal on the body of the shin, wet a linen cloth in cold water and place it on until the swelling subsides; and if the swelling is excessive, put crushed vitriol or galena on it, and similar things, until it subsides; or you place half-peeled beans on the wound and leave them there until they dry on the wound, which will stop the bleeding; and if you need more, take other shinbones.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the shinbones do not want to attach, rub the wound with fresh blood or insert a needle until the blood comes out, then place them on it, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; and when you see that they have stuck, sprinkle a little powder of aloe and crushed salt, or ash, on them, and they will adhere now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and deals with the repair of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know, dear son, that foolish doctors throw away this chapter, as they never saw any of the ancient books, nor did they read letters; and for this reason, knowledge is estranged in our land, for I never found any good one; and I know nothing, except through the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have extracted knowledge from it, and through experience, and through the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, and summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, as I did in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is thus necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise man directs his attention, and remains on the truth, so that those who have been tested may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when a fracture or dislocation or sprain occurs in someone, you should quickly heal the patient from one side and the other, if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of the body, children, old people; or if the time is not extremely hot or very cold; and eat dry foods, that is to say cold meats, and bird and hare meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you are certain there will be no hot abscess or spreading of matter to the limb; so that the patient returns to their usual regimen.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that make for thick nourishment, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and dairy products, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For through proper care, deformities and fractures are healed more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot heal or join together well according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs, nor can those who are too young, such as the bones of small children. But it doesn't matter, reset the broken bone and use large tongs that clamp down and bring the limb back together, as much as possible until it is restored to its original state. And do not prevent it from doing any of its work, and therefore it must be nourished with hearty foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse and varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the skull is different than that of the ribs or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes toward the armpit, and another one pointing, like the cut of a pen's feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture that is a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each type of break has its own tool and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory suggests in each case. The break in the bone is apparent when the place is twisted, and it can be felt clearly by pressing with the hand. But if there is no twisting or sound when touched, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break, but there may be a fracture or small break instead.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	And you should not move it by hand, but apply the following medications and then bind it gently.[Read More](https://www.engrade.com/browse/essay-topic-generator?title=Ancient+Medicine)
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the fractures that occur in branches, and are the two parts disjoined, they need to be aligned equally, so that pus does not come; and if pus comes, let it be for a few days, until the pus is pacified; then align it evenly as you can easily and neatly, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration of one where pieces are present; then bind it as required.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if the bone is broken into pieces, stretch it from two sides, whether it is an arm or a leg, or with your hand if it is a small member, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand; and place the member according to its natural form, so that when the parts of the member are separated, align all additions in their places as you can, and make sure that through your work the patient does not suffer injury or pain; and properly join the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And they can feel it with their hand if it doesn't seem to be in place: then straighten it nicely and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring about a hot and constricted abscess in the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is healed, chastise the patient well so that they do not move it, whether awake or sleeping, turning or in any other way; and ensure that the limb is secured so that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when they feel any pain, it is not yet healed, and one must put it in such a position that they feel no pain; and be careful to align it straight, so that there is no deformity when it is healed; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and in size and in shape."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small members, such as arms and hands and the like: these should be wrapped in soft and fine linen; and those that are large, such as hips and legs: these should be wrapped in a wide and firm binding, for the wide bindings embrace the entire limb and constrain it equally on all sides, so that there is no swelling; then wrap light stuffing around it three or four times according to the limb, and press your hand slightly on the entire binding, then go above the break and constrict less, so that the break moves apart slightly; and gradually loosen the binding until you encompass a great part of the healthy limb, then take another binding and wrap around again above the broken limb; then return to the part below the break, and constrict moderately, neither too tight nor too loose, as we have said in the first place above; then place linen or cloth stuffing between the bindings, so that it is all even; then bind it all with a bandage on top, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is swelling or abscess, place a warm compress that reduces the abscess and swelling, and leave it for several days; then apply traction using your ropes, with the incisions being half the width of a reed, or from a wooden stake used for fences, or from palm branches, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But it is necessary that the ropes placed on the fracture be slightly thicker and wider than the others; and also be as long as required for the size of the limb, whether small or large; then apply traction using your ropes as you did at the first location, then wrap a suitable thread over it as you did at the first location on the fracture; tighter is better, less so; and the thread should be of medium thickness, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen done by foolish people who make their own knots with twisted rope, this is a great error, because the knot cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not be less than two finger-widths between each rope.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the ends of the stitches after tightening in healthy places, place under them lint or wool padding, so that they do not wound themselves.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the bones are broken, I will tell you the treatment as follows.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to tighten with stitches all the fractured members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the member is large, there should be no application of ices, except after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on the certainty of an abscess arising; and here is the method of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations, and twisting: and it is that you take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and apply this concoction, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it in this way; and this is the common method of the restorative poultice for many types of fractures, and also for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of the restorative emplaster for healing fractures, dislocations, and twisting: take three parts of costmary, ladanum, elecampane, asafoetida, gum arabic, and myrrh; each part is ten drams; and four drams each of myrrh and aloes; and grind them into a powder, then mix with egg yolk; if the person's complexion is hot, use this emplaster as it has a good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and it benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another poultice method for twisting: take mugwort and masterwort, 10 deniers each; myrrh and aloes, 9 deniers each; acacia 6 deniers; and Armenian bole 10 deniers, and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another way to apply a plaster to dislocated joints and bones out of their place, and to alleviate the resulting pain, and for use in cutting or breaking the bone: take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not heal by itself, but it is good for alleviating the pain of a hot abscess and for removing pains properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of poultice that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and crushed broad-leaved thyme, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way to apply a plaster for the healing of bone fractures and for alleviating the remaining pain of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of madonna lily, chamomile, violet flowers, and bran in equal parts; grind and mix with wine, and if the limbs are hot, mix it with moist coriander water or plain water, and use it.[NOTE: The modern name for "vismalve" is althea officinalis or marshmallow root. Also, "veces" refers to bran or chaff.]
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another way of applying a plaster, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to restore the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of great mallow, and seeds of linseed, balm, melilot, and elderflower, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all of them one part; and crush, and make a paste with salt water, or soft water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not place anything on the broken member to restore it, except for a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be moderate in hardness, not too soft or too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen thinks that one should place on the broken member, to restore it, dry and slightly warm things, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another form of poultice that is good for wounds and pain: take a dog's mouth and chopped off men's hair, or bird feathers, and chamomile, and equally, grind them, and make a poultice and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then loosen it a little afterwards, and make sure the patient does not feel any pain, nor have the bones moved from their place; if there is pain in the area, or itching, without rest or swelling, hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth and sea sponge, soak in water, and raise the area, until the itching ceases and the pain is eased; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry wool, dampened with water or rose oil, and bind it up tightly, making sure that there is no heat from an abscess; and reduce inflammation of the member, and remove the pain, then carefully rebind it, and a little plaster, and do not tighten it as much as before; and gently continue until it heals.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the heated and red abscess and pain and swelling have all been removed, and you need poultice and bandages, then begin again as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no improvement comes to the limb from what we have said, do not unlock it before three days, or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on how it looks, until the break heals and the wound approaches coming together; then bind it more tightly than before, and the flesh will swell, as I said earlier; and if you see the wound drying out more than necessary, know that healing cannot come to it; then anoint it with warm water every time you unlock it, and this should be every third day, and loosen the bandage a little; by this work, healing comes to the limb, and quickly corrects what foolish doctors do, who incorrectly restore the limb; this is bad, and such work is to be feared, and I see no other option but to leave it alone and work on it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the different ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many types of fractures exist, with diverse shapes, and different causes; for there are fractures made by the striking of a sword, and the neck takes out all the bone down to the syphaxis which is beneath the bone, as done by a hatchet or stick; and this type of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or when the sword strikes the bone from above without penetrating, this type of fracture is called "absolue"; and the wound of these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a chip fracture, or a stone collar, or falling on a stone, or other similar things;
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a fracture that reaches up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that lodges in the bone as thin as a hair, and the break is small, it is therefore called this type of fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and forces the piece of bone inward, and the location is hairline, as when a blacksmith hammers on cauldrons; then it enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, such as that of a child; and it happens in all these types of fractures where small pieces are separated, like so; and I will speak of them later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the withdrawal (traction) on them, and the investigation using tensors, and by the decayed flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	A fracture is recognized by the appearance of hair when, after uncovering the bone and rubbing over it, a black line becomes visible.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be aware of the patient's condition and if you notice any adverse symptoms such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, paleness, feverish chills, eyes turning out and becoming red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it is unlikely to heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming symptoms and expect a recovery, then begin the treatment.[nitpicky]
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when a wounded person first comes to you in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month if possible.[nitpicky]
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the joint, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone does not become rotten, and the complications that we mentioned come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the fracture of the bone comes as far as the skin covering the brain, then you should split open the injured part in this way: take hold of the patient's injured head and expose the bone in all the ways that you can, as gently as possible on the surface of the wound; if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone or an abscess forms, help it with what is necessary; and it is done by filling the gap with cloths soaked in rose oil; let the wound rest until the abscess subsides and you are sure that there is no more bleeding; then begin to remove the bone, which is done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow incision in front, and this is the method.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put in another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and firm, then you must pierce it all around, so that you administer cuts with trephines, not so deep that they penetrate beyond the thickness of the skull, and there should be above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the tip to pass beyond the bone; and you need several of them, so that each one comes to rest in its place on the surface of the bone, so that you have trephines for all parts of the head; and this is the method of the three types of trephines.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The way to pierce around the bone is to place a trephine on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know that the bone is penetrated; then remove the trephine and place it in another spot nearby, and do this all around, then cut out the space of the skull between the holes with a chisel, doing this as delicately as possible and lightly, as we have said, so that you extract the bone by hand or with any of the tools that you have such as pliers or forceps; and be careful not to touch the brain or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced and treated the bone, you must remove the splinters that remain from the bone on all other similar instruments like a lancet, but it should be more slender and sharper than the other lancets; and if there are any small bones or scales left, gently remove them from the instruments; then cure the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen describes, which is safer; and he praises it highly, and this is his statement.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, it is necessary to uncover a portion of the bone in the place where the fracture is clearly visible. Once you have exposed that area, place the rounded tip of this surgical knife under the edge, as shown in its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not make a cut only on one side, and leave it ragged on both edges, so that the edge is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet so that you shave the bone all around, taking great care not to damage the cloth beneath; if it is adhered to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break of the bone does not penetrate through to the outer layer, and the bone is only cut through at the top, with small pieces, then you must smooth over that roughness, and remove the splinters with a sharp razor which you should have in various quantities, to make suitable adjustments in each place, according to the task and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	First use large razors, then smaller ones, and do not stop until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircutters and subtle breakers, it is necessary to make adjustments according to its alignment; and this is something that is not obvious to one who has devoted their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 And if the abscess is uncovered, you should take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another double cloth, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so as not to harm the abscess, then apply another ligament on top, but do not tighten it too much, just enough to hold the wound; and leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscess has calmed down, then loosen it and apply medicine such as lily roots, vetches flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and apply medicine that does not cause pain; and make sure that the wound stays clean, do not leave any residue or allow pus to accumulate, because when pus gathers on the cloth covering the brain, it will rot and cause great harm to the patient; because when you place something painful on the abscess, it will shrink and tighten, causing more damage.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any accident should befall the patient, as we have mentioned, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if no pus comes out except for what was caused by the medicine applied, and such virtue it has, then you should take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and soak a cloth in it, and place it on the abscess; then treat it with various treatments until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them alone, because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, it only swells or twists, and then heals.[Zapier generated this text automagically]
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should insert your little finger or the tip of your nostril, and align the break inside your index finger, and in front of it, until the nose returns to its natural shape; do this gently, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the knee, and the bone cannot come into place, then you should align it even with the end of a rod that is slightly thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the break is in two parts, then do the same thing, and hurry to restore it on the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed down, then place the tip of a linen cloth in the nostril, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or insert one (tent) from the other side if the fracture is there; and let the strips be so thick that they fill the hole(s) of the knee.[Note: The phrase "les pertus dou neis" could also be rendered as "the openings of the knee".]
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some surgeons say that you should moisten the bandages with butter and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It does not seem right to me, but it is necessary that they are moistened with a mixture of egg yolk and powdered flour; then leave the bandage on until the bone is healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes, one puts goose feathers in place of tenting, and with a soft cloth around, and the assistant holds it in place, and the patient blows through it; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses or pustules come on the nose while you are working, put on cerote (a type of medication) or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a patch of diachylon (an adhesive plaster).
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if abscesses do not form, apply an emplaster on top, made of sesame flour and powdered incense, mixed with egg yolk; then place light compresses on top, but do not bind it too tightly. If the fracture in the nose is small and broken into small pieces, extract them with appropriate instruments, then stitch the wound and cure any damage to the flesh and cartilage, as well as any abscesses and swelling, with appropriate ointments and emplasters. And if there is no wound inside the nostril, cure it with bandages and place wooden splints on it until it has healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jaw.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured but there is no wound outside, and the break is external only, without being broken in two, except for a small piece inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, then you should insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if it is on the left side, then insert your right hand's index finger, gently push the fracture inside, and align it with the other hand from the outside, making sure they are equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated into two parts, then you must administer extension to both sides until they are equal.[SIMULATE] Me: How did medieval medical practitioners diagnose a fractured jawbone?
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or a break, then bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a compress on the broken jaw, and place on it a double cloth; and place on the cloth a large star well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide to the jaw, and tie it to the chin as best you can, and command the patient to rest, and feed them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, then untie it on the third day, and then set right what has changed; and place a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with an abundance of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the compress; and place a light linen cloth on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it on until it heals; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, then use what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine if any piece of bone has been removed from it; then carefully remove it with the appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire as needed.

And when you have removed all those pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound if it is large, and apply a suitable poultice to it, to help heal the flesh until it is healed.

Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks several times before, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two pieces, and there are fragments, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.
