et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 and appears like a spoon, but is not curved, and should be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two edges, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, similar to the opening of the wound that you made when treating the bones; and when you are certain of a hot abscess, burn the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you suspect a hot abscess, bandage the wound with linen cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses appear, wet one linen cloth in rose oil, vinegar, and essential oil, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The setting of the bone, when there are no wounds or incisions, is done by placing poultice made from molin powder and egg white on the bone, and covering it with light wicks, and placing a sponge underneath if necessary; then take a large bandage one palm wide, place a double linen cloth over the wicks and poultice; then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around this bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs down; place the stick on the break, and wrap the bandage around the neck, under the healthy shoulder blade, and under the affected shoulder blade; bind each part, and when you see that the binding holds the break evenly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then rewrap it every day, and tighten it as the binding loosens; and have the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the affected shoulder blade to lift the shoulder up when they sleep; this will lighten the break by aligning the shoulder, or tying the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless there is an accident, for up to 20 days; then reapply the poultice if necessary, and bind and leave it in place until healed; and it is usually healed within 28 days, and sooner for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 Not often does the shoulder break or dislocate in such a way that it is noticeable from the outside, only perceptible through touch; align the shoulder according to the pattern of the break, and reset it according to its natural shape, in every way possible; then put powder of flour with plenty of egg, and light bandages, and place a double cloth on top; then place a wide and thin plate over it, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the plate in any part of the shoulder, fill those hairs with linen bandages, so that the plate fits evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, making sure the plate does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and whenever it softens, bind it again, and adjust the plate if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is accomplished, unbind it, and be careful, for it is not an easy thing if a bone comes out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone juts out in front, but not beneath the skin, then make an incision, and cut as we have said in the breakage of the forearm to pacify a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	In the break of the hip.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it breaks often at its end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and there is loss of blood, immediately, and perhaps they vomit blood, and the fracture is visible in the broken bone, and one can tell for sure.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration is as follows: the patient lies down with their back on a cushion placed between their shoulders, then you should press their shoulders and bring together their ribs using your hands, making sure to align all parts of the bone correctly; afterwards, apply poultices and bandages soaked in saltwater or another light wood over the fracture, wrap it in a cloth, and secure it firmly over the broken bone so that it does not move; then tie a bandage around their back, tighten it appropriately, and check every hour to see if it needs to be tightened again; if it becomes necessary to loosen the bandage due to infection, itching, pain, or abscess, do so quickly, remove the poultice, treat the affected area as needed, reapply a new poultice, and secure it until healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs does not come about except in heavy blows to the back, and at the chest within, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and one can feel it well upon examination of the sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the setting (or restoration) is to align the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 And then apply a poultice, and bind it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of ribs leans inward, then the patient feels great pain and distress, just like with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the skin; and there is sharp pain when breathing, and immediately there is a large flow of blood, which is a serious matter. Ancient physicians have applied much skill to this problem.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that one must administer food that causes the belly to swell in order to push the break outward.[0](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/aministrer)
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make it so that abscesses come to a boil, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come to a head, then lance it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should apply cups to the place in order to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cups may attract impurities to the place due to its weak constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the place with a cloth soaked in hot oil and then place bandages between the ribs to evenly apply pressure around, and then let it be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the break puncturing the cloth, and there is fear in the patient, then a cut must be made above the broken rib, and an instrument placed underneath to protect the lung; and then the bone must be sawn, and gently extracted, and then the edges of the wound sewn up if it is large, and treated with poultices until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if boils are about to come, put wet cloths with rose oil on it, and put it on the place; and care for the place as needed for the abscess, and lie down on your side where it is, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break/fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there occurs a break/fracture in the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if it will be healed or not, observe if you see their hands becoming softened, swollen, and numb, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortally afflicted in many ways, and if they can move and feel when they are pulled or poked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if treated.[note] I am not a medical professional, please consult with one for any health concerns.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will heal or not, observe if the feet are weak, and if there are symptoms in the hands, and on the back an involuntary windiness and discharge; and when it has been laid on its stomach, there is involuntary discharge.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is placed on its back and it wants to move, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is mortal: do not labor at all in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, then it is a less severe condition.[Reference(s):
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you should do if there is a hot abscess, place on it rose oil or egg yolk oil, until it is calmed down; then place one of the warming and drying plasters on it, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on the part where he feels pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone becomes dislocated, it is necessary to cover the area with a compress; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with one stitch, then cure it with a healing ointment, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", place your left hand pocket on it, and push it into place with your right hand to the best of your ability, then apply the plaster and bandage if needed; then bind it, and if there is a dislocated bone, adjust it and remove it, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the thigh bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the thigh bone is broken, and if it does, it rarely results in much narrowing at the end; it bends long and inclines outward, and causes pain to the patient in that area, and swelling and bruising in the area where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand on top, so that you are above the break; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is at the head only, then align that break equally, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or angulated inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, so that you can align the restoration of that break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have aligned it equally, then apply the poultice, and place a stick or wooden peg on top of it, holding the break in place so that it does not move; and apply a bandage beneath the ribs, until the swelling is equalized.[`json
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come from it, do not touch it until the arising abscess has calmed down, and apply what we have previously mentioned; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as is necessary, if no bad accident occurs; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint breakage
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is what lies between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a rod of medium size, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the shoulder joint with two bandages and pull them upwards, and place the patient on a seat; then let him rest his broken arm on the rod, so that it is in the middle of a bow-shaped piece of wood, then suspend it from some heavy object or have the attendant stretch it downward; then bring the two ends of the break together with your hands until the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is to position the patient on his backside, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants to hold either end of the broken bone with their hands, one holding the part above the break, and the other holding the part below, each pulling in their direction.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you want the extraction to be stronger, pull the ligament below the break, and above the break, and stretch out each of the helpers on their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the break is near the shoulder's top, you should place the middle band under the joint, and another one towards the groin, under the break; and also if the break is towards the groin, you should place a band lightly, without effort, until the break is aligned with the joint and the groin; then align the break as it should be, and bind it, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses do form, then do not apply tension for seven days, and place a wet linen cloth soaked in rose oil on the affected area. Wait until the abscess has calmed down, then apply tension. The method of applying tension is to place the poultice on the break, align the arm with the shoulder or chest, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest. Then place a cloth and apply tension on the shoulder and arm, so that the arm remains in its natural position, if nothing prevents it, and unless the bones are misaligned.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you are unsure whether the bones are misaligned, use a splint and place a wider and stronger rod over the break than the others, with a space of two fingers between each rod. Each rod should be large enough to extend beyond the break by three fingers on either side. Then apply tension to the rods as I described at the beginning of this chapter, more firmly and less gradually.[Additional context: This passage describes the use of a splint to stabilize and align a fractured bone before applying tension.]
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the swelling and tension, as we have said, at the time you restore the broken member, and you doubt an abscess will form, then leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the bandage every three days to see if there is itching, swelling, or redness in the area, or if circulation cannot reach the limb because the binding is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the procedure, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such accidents occur, do not loosen it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with hands over their stomach; place a cushion filled evenly with wool underneath the shoulder; and check every hour during the day or night to ensure that the position of the broken limb does not change or that the ligaments do not become too loose; then reset it using medical expertise, and provide them with food as previously mentioned, making sure that the food is initially light; and once they begin to recover, provide them with more substantial meals.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be reset in forty days total; and then one should loosen it and administer baths and ointments to help guide the limb back into place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the ligature is tight and embedded, it should remain to be untied for 3 days or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	Here's the translation of the text you provided in Old French about the treatment for a broken arm:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fosicles", one of which is small and is the one that follows the thumb; and the other is large and is the one that is below, towards the little finger; it may happen that only the large fosicle breaks, or only the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small ribs are broken, the restoration is easy, and so is the healing; but when the large ones are broken, the healing is difficult, and more painful than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If only the small ribs are broken, then they should be lightly stretched and aligned properly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large ribs that are broken, then they should be pulled harder; and place him on a cushion, holding the pouchet of his hand higher than the others, and the little fingers lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross himself over the cushion, with the cushion raised higher in front of him so that he feels no pain; then extend the arms of the attendants, one below at his side or to the ribs, and another attendant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then the doctor sets it evenly, in the best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break is in pieces, then place each piece in its proper location, and if there is any piece that is dislocated and pricks the heart, and you cannot reset it in its place, then cut and remove it as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken of this in a separate chapter; so treat it accordingly.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if in the beginning of the healing process abscesses appear, take a piece of soft cerote (plaster) made from oil of roses and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and gently apply it on top until the abscesses are calmed down.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the cerote and apply the poultice of powder from the mill with plenty of egg; put on the stylets (small pieces used in medical treatment), and make sure that the stylet of the fracture is stronger and slightly larger than the others; and know that it should have six stylets or branches, in multiple arrangements: whether the fracture is in one of the bones or two; and apply more pressure on the fracture than other parts, and lessen as you move away, as I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter; and make sure the bandages above the fracture are soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and use linen thread that is neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And reward the member and the ligament after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any bad accidents happen to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you should wet the member with hot water until the itching is calmed down; and let the member not be tightly restricted.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then resume the tightening, and if the ligaments are weakened and the bones disjointed, and similar things, treat it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that the circulation cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then you should soften it a little and leave it like that for several days, until the circulation has resumed, and then bind it again.[French to English translation by me, user: LaraCW](https://www.lotrbooks.com/userinfo.php?uid=62478)
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of the things that we have mentioned come to the patient, then do not release it until 20 days.[Note: I am a machine-learning model and my translations may sometimes be imperfect or lack nuance.
