ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 or around it, then bend his hands towards his neck, and make sure his collars are even, and beware of movement and loosening, and sleep on his back; and know that this breakage is healed in 30 days or 35, and perhaps even in 20 days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that breaks at the back of the hand and at the knuckles often occur, but they usually only result in bruising and not a break.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bruised, the patient should sit cross-legged and face straight ahead; then they should place their hand on a stretched out cloth, and the assistant should straighten the broken bones and align them properly until they are joined together; and apply a dressing and bandages, unless an abscess forms; then place a splint according to the size of the area; and wrap it in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is on the outer side around the stomach of the palm, then make a cushion out of cloth and instruct the patient to press it against their injured palm; then bind it with a long cloth, and make the splint out of wood as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside (dorsal side), then you must place a splint on top of it and another underneath in the palm, so that the hand remains open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and fasten the binding between the fingers.[IST] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the bone setter comes to one of our fingers, if it is crooked, he should straighten it as it should be; and hold it in place with the palm, and if you see fit, place a small, straight stick on top of the break to keep it from moving; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, he should straighten it and bind it to the healthy finger that follows; or you can bind them all together, making sure they are aligned, or you can place a stick on top, like a splint; and take care in the restoration and placement of hot abscesses, and help those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and it is clearly visible when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration consists of tying one ligature above the break, and another below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each assistant extends their ligature to their equal part; and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, let one of the ligaments be towards the wrist, and the other ligament below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And similarly if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be next to the knee, and the extension downwards; then place the surgeon's hands equally on both sides of the bone, until it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice and bind it, if pus does not form.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside and then return to your work and care; the ligature is made in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 It is necessary to wrap around the fracture a bandage doubled in two or three layers, and let the excess remain; then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, next to the knee below, and bring the ends of the thread to the top; then wrap around the leg and the thigh the bandage, then place a splint on the fracture, and place a splint on the bone of the leg; then apply soft cloths evenly between the thigh and the leg to make the tension equal, then begin to bind tightly three or four turns on the fracture; and as you go up the fracture, tighten less; then attend to the two ends of the thread that you put between the thigh and the leg, and tie them to the splints above, then return to below the head of the thread, so that you come next to the foot; and pull it tight, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, if there is no abscess, swelling or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess or swelling occurs, untie it and address what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they must be cut out if possible; and if not, the ligature must be cut and pulled out; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken so that steel pins are placed in it, as in the shoulder and arm; however, with this type of restoration, the patient is not made completely better.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in 3 days, or a little less or more, depending on the differences in complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin near the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the hollow of the knee there often occurs a small break, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is only a split or a hole, and this happens with all wounds, with or without an open wound, and it is easily felt.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that you put evenly what is dislocated at its two ends, until it can be moved as a whole; then apply the poultice, and place a round bandage if necessary, and bind it appropriately. Then, consider all the precautions that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar ones; and for each symptom, do what is necessary until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Here's the translation of the given Old French text into Modern English:
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called by its proper name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile". And it breaks in the same manner as it does in the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is also the same, and the work involved is identical. And if the two bones break together, the leg becomes deformed in all directions.[NOTE: The modern names for these bones are tibia (mustelz) and fibula (foscile).]
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, splint it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the large bone is broken, great pain is felt, and it is clearly visible; and it turns blue/black.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply traction and align it evenly, and bind the ends equally; but if the fracture is severe and there are multiple pieces, the traction should be less and lighter; and straighten it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two straps made of wood that encircle the leg on both sides and are as long as the leg from the knee downwards. Then wrap it in two layers, one above and one below, and tie it in the middle so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left; this is good. And some provide a stretcher made of wood for the leg to prevent movement, especially when there is an open wound in the fracture. Move the leg every day to check for signs of inflammation or other complications and continue treatment until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	"on the fracture of the leg bones" (lit. from the breaking of the leg bones)
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle is not prone to fractures, but sometimes the bones of the leg and foot are fractured in various ways, only resulting in bruising and dislocation without a break.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones of the foot break, and you see the bones sticking out over each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground as if they were going to walk, and then place your foot on top of theirs, where the bones are protruding. Then press hard until the bones return to their places; then apply a plaster and bandages, and under the belly of the foot, place a small board with two flat chips, then bind it to the foot after you have wrapped cloth around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the binding, for you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if some of the toes are broken, then set them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint on the broken toe according to the length of the toe, and it should be slightly wider, then place under the foot the board that I mentioned, and bind it to the foot. And if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the belly of the foot so that it supports it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have mentioned for other fractures, as we have said; and treat each injury as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the arm bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of the female womb is broken, have her sit with her legs spread apart, then lean her back and support it from behind; fill the vagina of the patient with cotton, as thick as a finger; then stand the woman up and lift her buttocks, causing the cotton to come out of the vagina and bringing the bone pieces together with the finger; when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton and replace it after she is done for seven days or so: the fracture will be healed. And if you wish, take a bladder of a cow and attach a reed to its opening, then insert the entire bladder into the vagina; blow strongly into the reed until the bladder fills inside; the bone pieces will come together; then fill with cotton and leave it like that for several days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the wrist in a man or woman is broken, it should be restored as we have said in the bone of the thigh; and such breaks are not hidden from one who applies close attention and skill, and pays heed to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For a break indicates in various ways the right path of restoration: pay attention therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloth around it and leave it for three days or so, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be healed now, so that the drainages that we have mentioned testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, apply vitriol to it if you have none otherwise, then begin to heal the fracture in that same hour or that day, unless abscesses come.[
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses do come, then leave the healing until the ninth day, until the abscess has calmed down, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad occurrence to happen.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears under the skin, exposed, then you must carefully align it with your hands, with slight extension.[
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not ready for you to place evenly on your hands, then realign it with this instrument which is made of iron, having 7 or 8 holes that are long, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the surgeon to press down 3 or 4 times, depending on what is needed in each fracture treatment; and it should be round and slightly thick, so that it does not bend during compression on the limb while you are working, and it should be sharp in front, and thick from the middle going forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche," which means that the curved joint should be placed on the end of the visible bone; and push it once, until it realigns, and make them even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the break is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone, then you must cut the end of the bone until the instrument has enough power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot realign the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, either a knife or saw, to your ability; and scrape away what remains in the bone, making it rough and removing small fragments.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Make sure it is in its place, then wet a cloth in black stiptic wine, and apply it properly if it is summer; and do not put any plaster or anything oily on the wound, as it may bring corruption and decay; then administer painkillers when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, cutting away the covering according to the size of the wound, taking care that the wound is not constricted by the break; and many times have foolish surgeons made this mistake, bringing death or infection upon the patient; and let the restraints be softer and milder than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is large or bad, and you fear that evil accidents may occur, as we have said, and find pain in the place, then soft bandages should not be applied; but instead, hard cloths should be wrapped around, in place of bandages, and tied.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after 1 or 2 days pus oozing from the wound, remove what you have placed on it, and apply a healing ointment, such as tetrapharmacon ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must unbind the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be bandaged in such a way that the swelling can easily go down.[Stripe text]
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if for many days it does not heal but instead keeps swelling up again, know that there are small bone fragments in the wound, which is why you must probe the wound with a tent and remove all the separated pieces causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, then you must cure it, according to what is said in its chapter earlier.[translating chapters, days etc as they are without implying anything specific]
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, do not pull it out, for many times this leads to death; but leave it until it rots. Perhaps it will come out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come on the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the health of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and it is an unpleasant sight to see the shape of the member; and perhaps the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if it is fresh for us: administer to him styptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, and similar others, so that you take one of these things, or all together, and cook them with a styptic wine or with egg white or with vinegar; and put it on the wound in rags, and bind it well, and do not loosen it for many days; and then loosen it and begin another, until the nodule is removed; or you can bind it tightly to a piece of wood well made; because the property of wood is that it removes all the swelling on the members; and if the nodule has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it off and let the excess appear; or have it shaved by a barber until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the weakened limb after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, but the limb remains weak and thin afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly and not properly; another reason is that there were too many bandages and the nourishment could not reach the limb; a third reason is excessive swelling; a fourth reason is due to excessive movement at the wrong time; or because the person has little blood in their body, making them weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you should feed the patient and make their body soft, causing blood to multiply in them; also administer baths for them and provide joy and pleasure. Then apply poultices on the limb so as to draw great nourishment to it, often moistening it with warm water until blood flows to the limb; and it returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the crooked limb after healing.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a limb is crooked after healing and the broken bone is clearly visible, but the form of the limb is ugly, it does not lose its natural function; do not believe those fools who say that the limb must be broken again, as many foolish doctors have done in our land; this procedure is to be blamed and leads to great harm, even possibly death. However, if the nodules and twisting are fresh, they should be soaked with warm water or softening herbs like leaves of mallow, roots, melilot, and similar things. Then make a softening poultice such as well-made daisy ointment, and take mallow sap, and blend it with goose fat or oil of lily, and apply the poultice; or use figs, mash them together with swine dung, and similar medicines that reduce hardening.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes nodes are removed through continuous and lengthy rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And bring about gentle movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisted parts (tortuositez) are wakened and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then it should be covered up to the bone, with a subtle incisor lightly; and place cushion and support in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs to someone, it must be returned immediately without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Because if one delays, the place becomes swollen, and perhaps it will not be reset properly; therefore, it is not good to move it when it is swollen: many times this brings on spasms and other pains. However, when this happens, make the patient vomit, then leave him alone until the abscess has subsided. Then apply warm water and oil to the limb, gently reset it, and treat each limb as it returns to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the jaw[STH: It seems like you are providing a single word answer, which is not in line with the previous translations provided. Here's a full translation of your input: "And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the jaw down to the feet."]
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It is rare for the jawbones to be dislocated on both sides, and there are two ways in which this can occur: either they are slightly out of their place and somewhat relaxed; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the back, causing saliva to flow from the mouth that cannot be held, and making it impossible to close the mouth and enveloping the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return to its normal position through several methods.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is whole and complete, you must quickly set it back, and do not delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and places his folded hand into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-sided; and let the other hand be free to adjust evenly; and command the patient to relax and move their jaw in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the physician should keep it aligned until it returns to its proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the reduction is difficult, even if it involves bringing together the two jaws, soak them with warm water and oil to gently realign it; do not delay in reducing it as we have said.[STHAPOR AND FEAR IN MEDIEVAL SURGERY]
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are evenly set back, and the mouth of the patient closes well without strain, then place wet bandages with a paste made of rose oil and wax on it, and bind it lightly with soft ligaments; and let the patient sleep on their back, and their head should be placed between two cushions so that it is not moved to the right or left, nor should they strive to chew, but eat light food until the pain subsides and the jaw heals; and then eat what you want lightly, and do not exert yourself to open your mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is fully healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be properly reset in an hour and are not returned to their proper place, then fever and chronic cough may follow, and perhaps stomach inflammation, and possibly vomiting of yellow bile.[Note: "solution de ventre" means inflammation of the stomach, "ventre" being an old word for belly or stomach. "Cole pure" is a term used to describe yellow bile.]
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a lost cause; and many times, those to whom it happens die within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork (or pitchfork)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be dislodged from the side and inside the ribcage, it is sometimes dislodged backwards, and one can certainly feel it.[Note: I am assuming that "li costeit" refers to the ribcage. If it actually means something else, then the translation might not make sense.]
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is that the patient lies flat on his back, and stretches out his arms; and then presses the area firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it; and the hip that is dislocated towards the edge cannot come out; if not, and if it comes out at any time, put it back in its place as we have said; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and similarly, the hip is put back in its place when it is dislocated from its joint.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder does not dislocate except in three ways: one of which is when it dislocates at the side towards the hip; and the second is towards the armpit; and perhaps it dislocates towards the top, but this happens rarely; and it never dislocates backwards towards the shoulder blade, nor inwards towards the nerves; and it often dislocates downwards towards the hip, especially for those who have little flesh, because it easily slips out; for those who have enough flesh, it slips out with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they experience a blow or fracture, and the shoulder becomes swollen with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.[NOTES:
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you should examine it until you are certain; and only then should you begin the cure.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it moves down towards the shoulder blade, creating a noticeable difference between the healthy and injured shoulder, and you will find a depression on the top of the shoulder, and below the shoulder blade when touching the top of the shoulder, just like an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his neck, nor make any movements; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for it can be clearly felt when touched; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to set back in place, especially when it is recent or when the child is the patient.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the assistant to lift the patient's hand up, then place your peaches (probably a tool) under the armpit, and forcefully lift the joint up to its place; and the assistant lifts the hand, extends it up, then puts it down. It will come into place quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come back as we have said, then the patient should be bathed in warm water, and given soothing and softening remedies, such as a decoction of clary, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and let them rest on their back; place a soft woolen cushion below the shoulder blade, not too hard or too soft, then have the patient put their heel on it and lift the top of their shoulder with force while pulling the patient's hand; and have another assistant hold the patient's head so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will come back immediately if done in this way: and it is necessary that a person who is stronger than the patient be present; stand by the patient's side, and push their shoulder blade down under the patient's shoulder blade, lifting the shoulder up so that the patient hangs from it; and have another assistant pull the patient's hand down towards their belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, have them hold something heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And the dislocation is also reset in another way: by inserting a long stake into the ground, so that the patient's head rests on it like a pillow, and it should not be too thick or too thin; then place it underneath the patient, but make sure they have soft cloths above, and the patient should be lying along the length of the stake; then stretch out their hand away from the other side strongly, and the joint will quickly return to its place; and if it does not want to return despite all the things we have mentioned, perform this treatment: take a stake that is two arms' lengths long and four fingers wide, with a pointed tip that can enter deep beneath the shoulder blade, in the following shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then place a soft cloth over the rod so that the rod does not injure the patient, and place it beneath the shoulder of the patient; extend their arm along the length of the rod, and tie the armpit to the rod, and their arm at the wrist of the hand, then place the arm on one step of a ladder of appropriate width, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body suspended in this way: the joint will return to its place now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, regardless of the method, you should put a wool sponge of equal size beneath the shoulder blade, then apply a plaster that is appropriate and powdered with flour of mill, with incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around it, then bind it appropriately beneath the shoulder blade, and turn the binding over the plaster, and embrace the hand to their neck, and let the hand remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that they eat lightly until the limb is healed, as it will heal more quickly in this way; and then eat more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, then you should apply cauteries to it at three openings, as is put forth in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this and it becomes dislocated again after seven days, and the joint will not hold and the arm cannot be raised, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder have been cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	A dislocation toward the side of the back and breasts, or to the rear, is caused by impact and extension of the hands, and another joint is used as a replacement; and it should be treated until it has healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes cracking in the limb and difficulty moving, then the patient should use baths many times until the cracking is relieved and returns to its normal state.[I'll translate the next sentence:] Et se il avient que par le coup ou autrement li malaides soit esvaniz, et devienne folz ou fous, si face tu decevior a lui de chose qe il se taiengne au mieux; et garde toi de lui faire chose dont il puisse estre plus empechié.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the rib(s)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated at points, and returns at points; and it has become dislocated all around, both in front and back, and the dislocation has not been reset, for it is clearly visible and can be felt; and it becomes dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick person with the knife to the wound, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way that abscesses will not come there, for if abscesses do come there, it will be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is in the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is as follows, when it is such that you can put it back, that you extend his hand with your two hands; and his arms be spread out, and the hands of the patient according to the cut around, above and below, and put the joint to its peaks together, or at the root of his palm, until it comes back to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm the cut that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 For if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong manipulation; and let two people hold the arm straight and pull on both sides so that it does not move during the extension; then bend the arm in each direction after you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it; and when the physician has aligned the joint with their hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly until it returns; and when it is back in place, apply dry ointment mixed with egg yolk and hold the arm tightly against the patient's chest, leaving it there for several days before releasing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is stable in its place, loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not holding well, reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it in this way for several days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels great pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is eased; or put some sheep's fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then replace the fat, and then enter the bath; and do this twice or three times, until it is healed; and if you wish, put moist cow dung, heated with butter, and bind it on; it will return to its place.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated and the return (to its original position) is easy, more so than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be quickly returned to its place in the same hour that it has become dislocated, so that the place is swollen, or a hot abscess comes.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the resetting is as follows: place the afflicted hand on a table, extend the assistant's hand, and the physician aligns it so that he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns to its place; however, you must ensure that it is in the correct position. Then, have the patient place the back of his hand on a table for the extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and let the doctor put his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it now returns (the dislocation), that is good. If not, bind it with emollient plasters for soothing abscesses and leave it like that without further movement.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot bear it and you cannot put it back in place after several days, then let the joint remain dislocated; and it will not harm the patient as long as the hand remains swollen and cannot be strained in any way: know that the nerves or arteries are cut; and there is no other remedy but to cauterize near the injury, and perhaps that will be of no use.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is healed, apply the plaster that we mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then unbind it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they cannot move it well, and there is any cracking sound, then moisten it with warm water and rub it until it heals.[STHILDE] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the thumbs of the hand

dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the small of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the small of the back or the neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death is swift for the patient.

des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that at the joints of the groin and the shoulder, there come only dislocations, not like the other joints; and the joint of the groin is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside than elsewhere, and less dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai. Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one for whom it comes on the outside is that these symptoms are contrary to those before.

And the signs of this that occurs to him in front, is that he stretches his leg according to the completion; nonetheless, he does not bend the knee without pain, and if he wants to make it move, he cannot advance, and he holds his urine, and his ankles swell, and when he walks, he steps on his heels.

Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it protrudes at the part where it is dislocated: the reduction is easy, and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is moved slightly.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is dislocated completely, you should make the patient sit upright, and hold them by the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and place the foot nicely upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, it is good; if not, start the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place a strong stick firmly in the ground between the thighs, and tie cloth around so that it does not hurt the patient; then hold the thigh with one assistant, and another assistant stretch the healthy leg with their hands or a ligament tied to the neck of the foot; then each assistant stretches evenly, and the stick should be firmly between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when they are stretched; then put the dislocation in its place with your hands, and another assistant hold the healthy leg down, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, put the poultice and wadding on, and bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if the bandage loosens, bind it again; then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for 4 days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses appear there, you should soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	The phrase "des dois" doesn't make sense on its own. It could be a part of a larger sentence or a medical term in Old French that I am not aware of. Could you please provide more context for this?
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without causing pain, and that is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any joint of the foot, you should make the patient sit upright on a level surface or on a table, and place your foot on the visible part of the joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns to its place; and when it is even, and there is nothing apparent, put a two-chambered board under the sole of the foot, then bind it firmly, and leave it for 3 days, then untie it; and let him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, often times it happens that the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not pitying and merciful and slow, not hasty; and use at the beginning soothing remedies for the swollen abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the swelling comes to it; and when the limb is in place, then administer soothing remedies for the hot abscess, and treat the wound, as is appropriate, with drying ointments; and if there is a fracture with the dislocation, and small bones are separated, then remove them, and do what we have said about simple diseases; and beware of entering the path of fear, as I have said, for it will lead you astray according to your Creator, and for the safety of your art and your body.
Amen	 Amen
